Mobile home stand means the improved site designed for the placement of a mobile home and its accessory structures, utility connections and off-street parking facilities. 
Modular home means an industrialized single-family dwelling which is manufactured in accordance with the applicable state law. Each unit must bear a seal of approval issued by the commissioner of the state department of community affairs (DCA). 
Recreational vehicle means a boat trailer and any type of portable structure without permanent foundations, which can be towed, hauled or driven and may be designed as temporary living accommodation for recreational, camping and travel use, and includes travel trailers, truck campers on or off the truck, camping trailers and self-propelled motor homes. 
Trailer means any vehicle or structure constructed so as to permit occupancy thereof as sleeping or living quarters, or the conduct of any business, trade or occupation, or use as a selling or advertising device, or use for storage or conveyance for chattel, tools, equipment or machinery, and so designed that it is or may be mounted on wheels and used as a conveyance on highways and streets propelled or drawn by its own or other motive power. The term "trailer" shall include, but not be limited to, automobiles, motorcycles, boat utility trailers, trailer coaches and mobile homes. 
Trailer, camping, means any portable structure or vehicle designed for highway travel at legal speed limits without a special permit which is intended for temporary living. 
(Code 1984, § 8-3-1; Code 1996, § 58-1)  
Sec. 32-2. - General requirements. 
(a)  Zoning compliance. All mobile homes, as well as mobile home parks within the city limits, shall comply with the city's comprehensive zoning requirements for location. Mobile home subdivisions will meet the minimum lot development standards for the zoning district in which the subdivision is to be located. 
(b)  Building and construction codes compliance. Any mobile home placed within the municipal limits of the city for a period exceeding 48 hours must bear an insignia issued by the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD). 
(c)  Health; water and sewer system regulations. Prior to the allowance of permanent occupancy of a mobile home within the city, the mobile home shall be connected with an approved water source, and an approved sewage disposal system in such a manner as to comply with the state department of public health and state water quality control board regulations and the state health code, which codes are, as insofar as applicable, hereby made a part of this chapter. 
(d)  Requirements for safety tie-downs. All mobile homes shall be provided with safety tie-downs in compliance with state laws and regulations. 
(e)  Frontage. All mobile homes, except in mobile home parks, shall generally face the street in which they are located. However, variations from this subsection may be allowed by the planning commission/city council if special lot considerations warrant a different street orientation. 
(f)  Skirting to enclose undercarriage. Within 30 days of installation, all mobile homes within the city must have a permanent skirt which completely encloses the undercarriage. Acceptable materials include masonry or stone and may include metal or other materials compatible with the siding of the particular mobile home unit. The mayor and council may specify the skirting material required for any particular permit application or for any skirting replacement at an existing home location. 
(g)  Permits required for accessory structures. Cabanas and other accessory structures shall require a building permit. 
(h)  Nonconforming mobile home. If a mobile home is removed from a nonconforming location or if it is destroyed beyond 50 percent of its fair market value, it shall not be replaced by another mobile home. 
(Code 1984, § 8-3-2; Code 1996, § 58-2)  
Sec. 32-3. - Use of trailer for permanent occupancy. 
Camping trailers shall not be used as a permanent place of abode or as a permanent dwelling or for indefinite periods of time; provided, however, that any camping trailer may be occupied and permitted in established mobile home parks for periods not exceeding 30 days. 
(Code 1984, § 8-3-3; Code 1996, § 58-3)  
Sec. 32-4. - Parking and location of trailers regulated. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful, within the limits of the city, for any person to park any trailer on any street, alley or highway, or other public place, or on any tract of land owned by any person, occupied or unoccupied, within the city except as provided in this chapter. 
(b)  One recreational vehicle may be parked or stored in an approved enclosed garage or in the rear yard of any lot on which an occupied dwelling is located, provided that no living quarters shall be maintained or business practiced in such recreational vehicle while it is so parked or stored. 
(Code 1984, § 8-3-4; Code 1996, § 58-4)  
Sec. 32-5. - Emergency and temporary stopping or parking. 
Emergency or temporary stopping or parking of trailers is permitted on any street, alley or highway for not longer than one hour, subject to any other and further prohibitions, regulations or limitations imposed by the traffic and parking regulations or ordinances for that street, alley or highway. 
(Code 1984, § 8-3-5; Code 1996, § 58-5)  
Sec. 32-6. - Location of mobile homes outside mobile home parks prohibited; exceptions. 
As specified in section 32-2, no person shall park or occupy any mobile home on the premises of any occupied dwelling or on any lot, except in compliance with the city's zoning ordinance or as provided by a permit approved by the mayor and council; provided, however, that mobile homes currently occupied as dwellings in the city outside established mobile home parks on the effective date of the ordinance from which this section was derived may continue to be occupied, but no such mobile home may be replaced by another mobile home without making application for a permit for the location of the new or replacement mobile home. 
(Code 1984, § 8-3-6; Code 1996, § 58-6)  
Sec. 32-7. - Location of accessory buildings or uses on residential lots. 
(a)  Accessory buildings may be erected in any required yard except a front yard. In no instance shall such a building be nearer than the required side yard for the principal building for the district in which it is located. 
(b)  In the case of double frontage lots, accessory buildings shall observe front yard requirements on both street frontages wherever there are any principal buildings fronting on such streets in the same block or adjacent blocks. 
(Code 1984, § 8-3-7; Code 1996, § 58-7)  
Sec. 32-8. - Accessory buildings or uses on nonresidential lots. 
Accessory buildings or uses on nonresidential lots shall comply with front, side and rear yard requirements established for the zoning district in which such accessory buildings or uses are located. 
(Code 1984, § 8-3-8; Code 1996, § 58-8)  
Sec. 32-9. - Mobile office. 
A mobile home may be converted and used as an office upon permission therefor duly issued by the building official, provided that no portion is used as a residential dwelling. Such permission shall contain such terms and conditions as deemed necessary by the building official. 
(Code 1984, § 8-3-9; Code 1996, § 58-9)  
Chapter 34 - NUISANCES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Nuisances, O.C.G.A. § 41-1-1 et seq.; jurisdiction of municipal court or magistrate court to abate nuisance, O.C.G.A. § 41-2-5. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 34-1. - Purpose. 
In order to eliminate unsightly, unhealthy or dangerous situations, and in order to protect property values and/or public health, and to enhance the beauty of the city, it shall be unlawful for any person to own, rent, lease or be in the possession of any premises, dwelling unit or other structure, place or vacant lot wherein the property is permitted to deteriorate in appearance or condition so as to be degrading to the surrounding premises, or be a threat to the public health. 
(Code 1984, § 11-2-6; Code 1996, § 42-31; Ord. of 5-7-1996(2), § 11-1-9(a))  
Sec. 34-2. - Conditions declared as nuisances. 
The following conditions may be declared to be nuisances: 
(1)  Stagnant water on a premises; 
(2)  Any dead or decaying matter, weeds, vegetation or any fruit, vegetable, animal or rodent, upon a premises, which is odorous or capable of causing disease or annoyance to the inhabitants of the city; 
(3)  The growth or maintenance of tall grass, weeds and bushes, and other undergrowth on the premises; 
(4)  The accumulation or maintenance of trash and debris of any type, dilapidated furniture, appliances, machinery, equipment, nonmotorized vehicles or old or discarded tires on the premises; 
(5)  The generation of smoke or fumes in sufficient amount to cause odor or annoyance to the inhabitants of the city; 
(6)  The pollution of public water or the injection of matter into the sewage system which would be damaging thereto; 
(7)  Maintaining a dangerous or diseased animal or fowl; 
(8)  Obstruction of a public street, highway or sidewalk without a permit; 
(9)  Loud or unusual noises which are detrimental or annoying to the public, including, without limitation, unusual loud disturbances in or around churches or multiple-family complexes, such as loud music and other activities in swimming pool and clubhouse areas; 
(10)  All walls, trees and buildings that may endanger persons or property; 
(11)  Any business or building where illegal activities are habitually and commonly conducted in such a manner as to reasonably suggest that the owner or operator of the business or building was aware of the illegal activities and failed to reasonably attempt to prevent those activities; 
(12)  Unused iceboxes, refrigerators and the like unless the doors, latches or locks are removed; 
(13)  Any trees, shrubbery or other plants or parts thereof, which obstruct clear, safe vision on roadways and intersections of the city; and 
(14)  Any other condition constituting a nuisance under state law. 
(Code 1984, § 11-2-1; Code 1996, § 42-32; Ord. of 5-7-1996(2), § 11-1-9(b))  
Sec. 34-3. - Jurisdiction of municipal court to try and punish. 
The municipal court shall have full jurisdiction to try and dispose of all questions of nuisance affecting the public health or welfare, and shall also have jurisdiction to try and, upon conviction, to punish persons failing to abate nuisances, as prescribed in section 1-11. 
(Code 1984, § 11-2-2; Code 1996, § 42-33)  
Sec. 34-4. - Notice to offenders; service; failure to comply; bringing of charges. 
Should the city manager, or his designee, determine that any person is violating the terms of this chapter, the city manager, or his designee, shall give the offending party 15 days' notice within which to eliminate the unsightly, unhealthy or dangerous situation. This notice shall be in writing and shall be served upon the owner and occupant of the premises. If the occupant is not the owner, then the owner shall also be notified. The service or notice may be made either in person or by mail. Should the person to whom the notice is directed fail to comply with the request made therein within the 15-day period, the city manager, in cooperation with the city attorney, shall be authorized to proceed with the bringing of charges for the violation, pursuant to O.C.G.A. §§ 41-2-2 and 41-2-5. Each day the conditions continue shall be deemed a separate offense. 
(Code 1984, § 11-2-3; Code 1996, § 42-34; Ord. of 5-7-1996(2), § 11-1-9(c))  
Sec. 34-5. - Abatement following conviction; liability for costs; lien; enforcement. 
Pursuant to the judgment of the municipal court, the city may, at its option, proceed to remedy the unsightly, unhealthy or dangerous situation, and accomplish the necessary work. The owner or occupant, or both, shall be liable for the actual cost of such work, and the actual cost of such work shall be assessed against the property owner upon whose premises the work is done, and if the bill for such charges remains unpaid for 30 days after it has been rendered, such cost shall become a lien upon the premises, enforceable in the same manner as provided for the collection of unpaid taxes. 
(Code 1984, § 11-2-4; Code 1996, § 42-35; Ord. of 5-7-1996(2), § 11-1-9(d))  
Sec. 34-6. - Nuisance per se; exception; summary abatement. 
Nothing contained in this chapter shall prevent the mayor from summarily and, without a notice, ordering the abatement of any nuisance that is a nuisance per se in the law, or where the case is an urgent one and the health and safety of the public or a portion thereof is in imminent danger. 
(Code 1984, § 11-2-5; Code 1996, § 42-37)  
Secs. 34-7—34-30. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - ABANDONED AND JUNKED MOTOR VEHICLES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Authority to provide by ordinance for removal and disposal of junked vehicles, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-4. 
 
Sec. 34-31. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Abandoned vehicle means a machine designed to be propelled by an internal combustion engine, or by an electric motor, manufactured for the transporting of persons or property, including, without limitation, automobiles, trucks, truck trailers, motorized carts, motorcycles, mopeds, scooters and tractors, which is in an inoperative state because of being wrecked, junked, dismantled, unused or discarded. In instances where a machine is subject to this article, and is required to have a valid license issued by the state, or any other state, for operation on the public streets of this state, the absence of the required evidence of a valid and current license displayed on the machine shall constitute, for the purposes of this article, a prima facie showing that the machine is in an inoperative state. 
Enclosure means a structure constructed or manufactured in a manner so as to preclude any view of any portion of the interior thereof from any public street or sidewalk. For the purposes of this article, a custom vehicle cover, specifically designed, manufactured, created or constructed to provide, for the life of the product, permanent protection for a motorized vehicle from the adverse effects of the weather, shall be deemed to be an enclosure; provided, however, that such definition shall not be deemed to include tarpaulins and other similar products which are not specifically designed, manufactured, created or constructed to provide protection solely for a motor vehicle from the adverse effects of the weather, and are ordinarily and customarily used only to provide temporary protection from such adverse effects. 
Residential property means any real property located within the city designated under the zoning ordinances and maps as residential zoning districts, or any real properties located within the city which are primarily utilized to provide living quarters for one or more individuals. 
Storage means the parking or leaving of an abandoned vehicle for a period of time in excess of five consecutive days. 
(Code 1996, § 42-56)  
Sec. 34-32. - Storage on residential property. 
(a)  No person in charge or control of any residential property located within the city, whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee, or otherwise, shall cause or allow any abandoned vehicle to be or remain in storage in or on the front yard area of such residential property unless the abandoned vehicle is wholly contained in an enclosure. The front yard shall be determined as the portion of any lot designated as being within the required front yard setback or building line as determined by the city's zoning regulations. 
(b)  No person in charge or control of any residential property located within the city, whether as owner, tenant, occupant, lessee, or otherwise, shall cause or allow any abandoned vehicle to be or remain in storage in or on the side yard area or rear yard area of such residential property unless the abandoned vehicle is wholly contained in an enclosure. The side and rear yard shall be determined as the portion of any lot designated as being within the required side or rear setback or building line as determined by the city's zoning regulations. 
(Code 1996, § 42-58)  
Sec. 34-33. - Declaration of nuisance. 
(a)  Pursuant to the authority granted to the city under the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 36-60-4, the mayor and council of the city has concluded that any abandoned vehicle kept or maintained in violation of the provisions of section 34-32 constitutes a health hazard or unsightly nuisance, and any person responsible for creating or permitting the continuance of such a nuisance shall have ten days from the date of written notice of such nuisance to either remove the abandoned vehicle from the residential property or to provide such storage or maintenance thereon as will effectuate compliance with the directives thereof. If the person either fails or refuses to remove the abandoned vehicle from the residential property, or to bring the abandoned vehicle in compliance with the directives of section 34-32, within the ten-day period, then the continued presence of the abandoned vehicle on the property shall constitute misdemeanor. Any violation of section 34-32 not cured within the notice period may be abated pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 40-2-5 and section 34-34. 
(b)  Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 36-60-4, any abandoned vehicle kept or maintained in storage on private property within the city, whether the property be used for residential, commercial, agricultural or industrial purposes, and excepting only a junkyard complying with the laws of this state, where the storage of the abandoned vehicle constitutes a health hazard or unsightly nuisance shall be subject to the abatement proceedings provided in section 34-34, after the notice and ten-day cure period have been provided as set forth in subsection (a) of this section. 
(Code 1996, § 42-59)  
Sec. 34-34. - Proceeding for nuisance abatement. 
(a)  As provided in O.C.G.A. § 41-2-5, the jurisdiction for the abatement of any nuisance arising out of the existence of an abandoned vehicle located on private property within the city shall be vested in the municipal court. The grant of jurisdiction made in this section is not intended, and shall not be construed to be, a grant to exclude or limit the jurisdiction of any other court of this state vested by the law of this state with jurisdiction over such proceedings. 
(b)  Any proceeding to abate a nuisance existing or resulting from an abandoned vehicle in storage on private property within the city shall be commenced by the chief of police of the city in the name and on the behalf of the city, or by a private citizen thereof, by the filing of a petition with the municipal court seeking the abatement thereof. The petition shall identify the property upon which the abandoned vehicle is being maintained, state the name of the person in control or possession of the real property, together with a description of the abandoned vehicle alleged to constitute such nuisance, and shall provide sufficient facts so as to inform the court as to the nature of such nuisance. If, upon the filing of such petition, the judge of the court concludes that sufficient facts are alleged to require further inquiry and proceedings as to the existence of a nuisance, an order shall be entered by the court setting a hearing date for the adjudication of the issues raised in the petition. 
(c)  The petition to abate the nuisance, together with a copy of the order of the court for hearing thereon, shall be served on the person in possession or control of the real property upon which the nuisance is alleged to exist at least ten days prior to the scheduled hearing date, either personally or by certified or registered mail with return receipt requested. If either the identity or location of such person is unknown, or for whatever reason such person cannot be located for such service, a copy of the petition and the order shall be conspicuously affixed to the abandoned vehicle in a manner so as to provide anyone in its vicinity with notice of the presence of such petition and order. 
(d)  At the scheduled hearing, the court shall hear the pertinent evidence as to the facts and circumstances surrounding the maintenance of the abandoned vehicle and shall allow the person in possession or control of the real property to present any relevant and pertinent evidence as to why same does not constitute a nuisance. 
(e)  If after hearing the evidence presented at the hearing the court concludes that a nuisance, within the meaning of section 34-33, exists, the court shall enter an order requiring and directing that the abandoned vehicle be removed from the corporate limits of the city within ten days of the date of the order. A copy of the order requiring the abatement of the nuisance shall be served on the person in possession or control of the real property upon which the nuisance is alleged to exist, either personally or by certified or registered mail with return receipt requested. If either the identity or location of such person is unknown, or for whatever reason the person cannot be located for the purposes of such service, a copy of the order shall be conspicuously affixed to the abandoned vehicle in a manner so as to provide anyone in its vicinity with notice of the presence of the order. 
(f)  If the person in control or possession of the property upon which the abandoned vehicle exists fails to remove the abandoned vehicle within the ten-day period specified by the court for the abatement of the nuisance, then and in such event the city shall remove, or cause to be removed, the abandoned vehicle from the municipal limits of the city for disposal in such a manner as will terminate the characteristics thereof which resulted in same being found to be a nuisance. The city, in the pursuit of its duties to dispose of the abandoned vehicle, shall be authorized to sell the abandoned vehicle for junk or metal salvage, and any consideration received for such sale shall be retained by the city to offset the costs and expenses incurred in the abatement of the nuisance. 
(Code 1996, § 42-60)  
Secs. 34-35—34-56. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - NOISE CONTROL[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Limits on sound volume produced by a radio, tape player or other mechanical sound-making device or instrument from within a motor vehicle, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-14; sale of muffler which causes excessive noise prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 40-8-71(c). 
 
Sec. 34-57. - Loud and unnecessary noises. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to make, continue or cause to be made or continued any loud, unnecessary or unusual noise or any noise which unreasonably or unnecessarily annoys, disturbs, injures or endangers the comfort, repose, health, peace or safety of others in the city. The chief of police, or his designee, may issue a citation for any violation of this article. 
(Code 1984, § 11-1-4(a); Code 1996, § 42-121)  
Sec. 34-58. - Exemptions. 
The provisions of this article shall not apply to or be enforced against: 
(1)  Any vehicle of the city while engaged in necessary public business; 
(2)  Excavations or repairs of streets by or on behalf of the city, county or state at night when public welfare and convenience renders it impossible to perform such work during the day; or 
(3)  The reasonable use of amplifiers or loudspeakers in the course of public addresses which are noncommercial in character, if permission has been obtained from the mayor and council. 
(Code 1984, § 11-1-4(b); Code 1996, § 42-122)  
Sec. 34-59. - Certain acts deemed prohibited noises. 
The following acts, among others, shall constitute a violation of section 34-57, but such enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive: 
(1)  Horns and signaling devices. The sounding of any horn or signaling device on any automobile, motorcycle or other vehicle on any street or public place in the city, except as a danger warning; the creation of any unreasonably loud or harsh sound by means of any such signaling device and the sounding of any such device for an unreasonable period of time; the use of any signaling device, except a police whistle or one operated by hand or electricity; the use of any horn, whistle or other device operated by engine exhaust and the use of any such signaling device when traffic is held up for any reason. 
(2)  Radios, phonographs and other machines which produce or reproduce sound. The playing, using or operating, or permitting to be played, used or operated, of any radio receiving set, musical instrument, phonograph, tape recorder, cassette player, CD player, or other machine or device for the production or reproducing of sound in such manner as to disturb the peace, quiet and comfort of the neighboring inhabitants or pedestrians within any area of the city, or at any time with louder volume than is necessary for convenient hearing for the person who is in the room, vehicle, place or chamber in which such machine or device is operated, and who is a voluntary listener thereto. The operation of any such set, instrument, phonograph, tape recorder, cassette player, CD player, machine or device in such manner as to be plainly audible at a distance of 50 feet from the building, structure, place or vehicle in which it is located shall be prima facie evidence of a violation of this section. 
(3)  Loudspeakers and amplifiers for advertising. The playing, using or operating, or permitting to be played, used or operated, of any radio receiving set, musical instrument, phonograph, loudspeaker, sound amplifier or other machine or device for the producing or reproducing of sound which is cast upon the public streets for the purpose of commercial advertising or attracting the attention of the public to any building or structure without a special permit from the city clerk or governing authority. Announcements over loudspeakers can only be made by the announcer in person and without the aid of any mechanical device. 
(4)  Yelling and shouting. Yelling, shouting, hooting, whistling or singing on the public streets, particularly between the hours of 11:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m., or at any time or place so as to annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of any persons in the vicinity. 
(5)  Animals and birds. The keeping of any animal or bird which will disturb the comfort or repose of any persons in the vicinity by making loud, continual or frequent noise. 
(6)  Steam whistle. The blowing of any train whistle or steam whistle attached to any stationary boiler, except to give notice of the time to begin or stop work or as a warning of fire or danger or upon request of proper city authorities. 
(7)  Exhausts. The discharge into the open air of the exhaust of any steam engine, stationary internal combustion engine, motorboat or motor vehicle, except through a muffler or other device which will effectively prevent loud or explosive noises therefrom. 
(8)  Defect in vehicle or load. The use of any automobile, motorcycle or vehicle so out of repair, so loaded or in such manner as to create loud and unnecessary grating, grinding, rattling or other noise. 
(9)  Loading, unloading and opening boxes. The creation of a loud and excessive noise in connection with loading or unloading any vehicle or the opening and destruction of bales, boxes, crates and containers. 
(10)  Construction or repairing of buildings. The erection (including excavating), demolition, alteration or repair of any building other than between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. on weekdays, except on urgent necessity in the interest of public health and safety, and then only with a permit from the city building official, which permit may be granted for a period not to exceed three days or less while the emergency continues and which permit may be renewed by the mayor and council for periods of three days or less while the emergency continues. If the council determines that the public health and safety will not be impaired by the erection, demolition, alteration or repair of any building or the excavation of streets and highways from 6:00 p.m. to 7:00 a.m., and further determines that loss or inconvenience would result to any party in interest, the council may grant permission for such work to be done from 6:00 p.m. to 7:00 a.m., upon application made at the time the permit for the work is applied for or during the progress of the work. 
(11)  Noise causing disturbance to schools, courts, churches and hospitals. The creation of any excessive noise on any street adjacent to any school, institution of learning, church or court while such institutions are in session or adjacent to any hospital, and which unreasonably interferes with the work of such institution, or which disturbs or unduly annoys patients in the hospital; provided, however, that conspicuous signs are displayed about such institutions indicating the presence of such institutions. 
(12)  Hawkers, peddlers and vendors. The shouting and crying of peddlers, hawkers and vendors which disturb the peace and quiet of the neighborhood. 
(13)  Noises to attract attention; use of drums and other instruments. The use of any drum or other instrument or device for the purpose of attracting attention to any performance, show or sale by creation of noise. 
(14)  Transportation of metal rails. The transportation of rails, pillars or columns of iron, steel or other material over and along streets and other public places upon carts, drays, cars, trucks or in any other manner so loaded as to cause loud noises or as to disturb the peace and quiet of such streets or other public places. 
(15)  Piledrivers, hammers or other loud appliances. The operation from 6:00 p.m. to 7:00 a.m. of any piledriver, steam shovel, pneumatic hammer, derrick, steam or electric hoist or other appliance, the use of which is attended by loud or unusual noise without a special permit from the mayor and council. 
(16)  Blowers. The operation of any noise-creating blower or power fan or any internal combustion engine, the operation of which causes noise due to the explosion of operating gases or fluids, unless the noise from such blower or fan is muffled and such engine is equipped with a muffler device sufficient to deaden such noise. 
(17)  Sound trucks. The use of mechanical loudspeakers or amplifiers on trucks or other moving or standing vehicles for advertising or other commercial purposes, and the use of sound trucks for noncommercial purposes during such hours or in such places or with such volume as would constitute such use a public nuisance. 
(Code 1984, § 11-1-5; Code 1996, § 42-123; Ord. of 4-2-1991)  
Chapter 36 - OFFENSES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Limitation on home rule powers of municipal corporations with respect to duplication of state criminal offenses, O.C.G.A. § 36-35-6(a)(2). 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 36-1. - Public drunkenness. 
It shall be unlawful for any person within the city to be and appear in an intoxicated condition upon any street or sidewalk of the city or in any other public place or private business premises patronized by the public, when such condition results in boisterous, disruptive or annoying behavior which interferes with the lawful pursuits of others. 
(Code 1984, § 11-1-7; Code 1996, § 62-1)  
Sec. 36-2. - Drinking in public. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to consume any spirituous malt or alcoholic beverage while a pedestrian in or upon any street, alley, sidewalk or other public way or place within the city, or within any public building. 
(Code 1996, § 62-2)  
Sec. 36-3. - Loitering or prowling. 
The offense of loitering or prowling, as defined in this section, within the city is hereby declared unlawful. A person commits the offense of loitering or prowling when he is in a place at a time or in a manner not usual for law-abiding individuals under circumstances that warrant a justifiable and reasonable alarm or immediate concern for the safety of persons or property in the vicinity. Among the circumstances which may be considered in determining whether alarm is warranted is the fact that the person takes flight upon the appearance of a law enforcement officer, refuses to identify himself, or manifestly endeavors to conceal himself or any object. Unless flight by the person or other circumstances make it impracticable, a law enforcement officer shall, prior to any arrest for the offense, afford the person an opportunity to dispel any alarm or immediate concern which would otherwise be warranted by requesting the person to identify himself and explain his presence and conduct. No person shall be convicted of this offense if the law enforcement officer failed to comply with such procedure or if it appears at trial that the explanation given by the person was true and would have dispelled the alarm or immediate concern. 
(Code 1996, § 62-3) 
State Law reference— Loitering or prowling, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-36; ordinances proscribing loitering or related activities not preempted, O.C.G.A. § 16-6-24.  
Sec. 36-4. - On-premises sales of personal property. 
(a)  For the purposes of this section, the term "on-premises sale" shall be construed to mean any public sale or public offering for sale of any personal property by any person on premises located in a geographical area of the city zoned other than commercial, or grandfathered for commercial use, at which sale such property is publicly displayed for sale to the public at large. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful to hold any on-premises sale at a location other than at premises owned or occupied by the holder thereof. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person to hold more than two on-premises sales at any one location during any 12-month period. 
(d)  Any on-premises sale shall not be operated in such a manner as to cause a nuisance to neighboring residences or in such a manner as will create a fire hazard or traffic hazard or pose any other significant risk to public safety. 
(Code 1996, § 62-4)  
Sec. 36-5. - Public indecency prohibited. 
(a)  A person commits the offense of public indecency when he performs any of the following acts in a place where a person should reasonably expect to be in view of the public: 
(1)  An actual or simulated act of sexual intercourse or masturbation; 
(2)  Exposure of the genitals; 
(3)  A lewd appearance in a state of partial or complete nudity; 
(4)  A lewd caress or indecent fondling of the body of another person; 
(5)  A lewd caress or indecent fondling of the sexual organs of any person, including oneself; 
(6)  Urination or defecation; or 
(7)  Appears wearing pants or shirts more than three inches below the top of the hips (crest of the ilium), exposing the skin or undergarments. 
(b)  Fines and penalties. A citation shall be issued to the offender and the person shall be subject to penalty according to section 1-11. The person shall be subject to a penalty of not less than $50.00 on the first offense and an increasing penalty for each subsequent offense at the discretion of the court or from a chart of fines that is approved by the judge of the municipal court of the city. The person may also be subject to community service activities for violation at the discretion of the court, or to both monetary fine and community service. 
(Ord. of 6-7-2011, § 1(62-5))  
Secs. 36-6—36-28. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC PEACE 
 
Sec. 36-29. - Disorderly conduct. 
Any person who shall do or engage in any of the following in the city shall be guilty of disorderly conduct: 
(1)  Act in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another, whereby any person is placed in danger of safety of his life, limb or health. 
(2)  Act in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another, whereby public property or the property of any other person is placed in danger of being destroyed or damaged. 
(3)  Endanger lawful pursuits of another by acts of violence or threats of bodily harm. 
(4)  Cause, provoke or engage in any fight, brawl or riotous conduct so as to endanger the life, limb, health or property of another or public property. 
(5)  Assemble or congregate with another and cause, provoke or engage in any fight or brawl. 
(6)  Collect in bodies or in crowds and engage in unlawful activities. 
(7)  Assemble or congregate with another and engage or attempt to engage in gaming. 
(8)  Frequent any public place and obtain money from another by an illegal and fraudulent scheme, trick, artifice or device, or attempt to do so. 
(9)  Use fighting words directed towards any person who becomes outraged and thus creates turmoil. 
(Code 1996, § 62-31)  
Sec. 36-30. - Obstructing city officer in discharge of duties. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to hinder, delay or obstruct or prevent any officer employed by the city, or any person acting for or under the direction of such officer, from performing any act which by reason of his office or position may devolve upon such officer or person. 
(Code 1984, § 11-1-6; Code 1996, § 62-32)  
Secs. 36-31—36-48. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC SAFETY 
 
Sec. 36-49. - Weapons. 
It shall be unlawful to have, possess or carry upon the streets, alleys or sidewalks of the city any of the following implements, unless the implements are securely wrapped so as not to be readily available for harmful use: 
(1)  Any knife which has a blade which opens automatically by hand pressure applied to a button, spring or other device in the handle, the blade of which, when open, projects from the handle two inches or more. 
(2)  Any knife which has any obstruction or other device of any kind which holds the blade partly open, the blade of which, when open, projects from the handle two inches or more. 
(3)  Any knife of any kind, the blade of which, when open, projects from the handle more than three inches. This is intended to include all knives such as butcher knives or other knives which do not close. 
(4)  Any straight razor. 
(5)  Any icepick or similar device having a sharp point, except this shall not apply to any person delivering ice. 
(Code 1984, § 11-1-8; Code 1996, § 62-61)  
Sec. 36-50. - Airguns or slingshots; use upon city streets, sidewalks or lots. 
No person shall use a sling or slingshot or airgun upon the streets, sidewalks or lots of the city. 
(Code 1996, § 62-62)  
Sec. 36-51. - Firearms; discharge. 
No person shall fire any gun, pistol or any firearm within the city limits, except law enforcement officers when acting in the performance of their official duties. 
(Code 1996, § 62-63) 
State Law reference— Discharge of firearm near public highway or street, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-103; discharge of firearm on property of another, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-104; discharge of firearm on Sunday, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-105; Georgia Firearms and Weapons Act, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-120 et seq.  
Secs. 36-52—36-75. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC PROPERTY[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Damaging, injuring or interfering with utilities, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-25. 
 
Sec. 36-76. - Damaging or defacing property. 
It shall be unlawful to deface, mar or damage, or, without proper authority, to write, carve, paste or print any marks, letters or pictures on any public or private property in the city. 
(Code 1984, § 11-1-2; Code 1996, § 62-91)  
Sec. 36-77. - Digging ditches; pushing up and removing trees on city property. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to dig or cause to be dug any ditch or to remove or push up trees located or standing on city property unless permission has been obtained from the mayor and council. 
(Code 1984, § 11-1-3; Code 1996, § 62-92)  
Sec. 36-78. - Blocking public passages and ways. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to loiter or stand on any street, sidewalk or curb in such a manner as to render the same unsafe or unsuitable for the passage of persons and the transportation of commodities or in such a manner as to limit the peaceful and tranquil use of such streets, sidewalks or curbs by the public at large. Any such person shall move on or separate when required to do so by any member of law enforcement and shall cease to occupy such position on the street, sidewalk or curb of the city. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to loiter or stand in or on any public place in the city, including its public places, such as alleys, parks, playgrounds, recreational areas, public lawns and walkways and public buildings, in such a manner as to render the same unsafe or unsuitable for the use of the same for their proper purposes by members of the general public or in such a manner as to limit the peaceful and tranquil use of such public places by the public at large. Any such person shall move on or separate when required to do so by any member of law enforcement and shall cease to occupy such position in such public place of the city. 
(Code 1996, § 62-93)  
Sec. 36-79. - Utilities apparatus; public or private. 
It shall be unlawful for any person intentionally and without authority to injure or destroy any meter, pipe, conduit, wire, line, post, lamp, or other apparatus belonging to a company, municipality or political subdivision engaged in the manufacture or sale of electricity, gas, water, telephone or other public services; intentionally and without authority to prevent a meter from properly registering the quantity of such service supplied; in any way to interfere with the proper action of such company, municipality or political subdivision; intentionally to divert any services of such company, municipality or political subdivision; or otherwise intentionally and without authority to use or cause to be used, without the consent of the company, municipality or political subdivision, any service manufactured, sold or distributed by the company, municipality or political subdivision. 
(Code 1996, § 62-94)  
Sec. 36-80. - Responsibility for acts of tampering or diversion. 
Where there is no evidence to the contrary, the person performing any of the illegal acts set forth in section 36-79, and the person who, with knowledge of such violation, receives the benefit of such service without proper charge as a result of the improper action, shall be presumed to be responsible for the act of tampering or diversion. 
(Code 1996, § 62-95)  
Sec. 36-81. - Outdoor advertising on city property. 
(a)  No person shall place any outdoor advertising on any property owned by the city, except as provided in subsection (c) of this section. 
(b)  For the purpose of this section, the term "outdoor advertising" shall include, but not be limited to, signs, posters, handbills, banners, paintings or any visual means of representing words or ideas, as well as the use of amplifiers, musical devices or loudspeakers on public property to promote a particular business or product. 
(c)  Advertisements concerning nonprofit events open to the public may be placed on public property following approval by the mayor and council. Such advertisements shall be subject to all conditions imposed by the council concerning the number, size, location and duration. 
(Code 1984, § 9-1-1; Code 1996, § 62-97)  
Secs. 36-82—36-105. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE V. - CURFEW FOR MINORS 
 
Sec. 36-106. - Imposed. 
It shall be unlawful for any minor under the age of 18 years to loiter, idle, wander, stroll or play in or upon the public streets, highways, roads, alleys, parks, playgrounds or other public grounds, public places or public buildings, places of amusement or entertainment, eating places, vacant lots or any other places normally accessible to the general public for public use, whether on foot or in a motor vehicle or by any other means, during the following periods of time: 
(1)  For minors age 15 years and under, between the hours of 10:30 p.m. on any day and 6:00 a.m. of the following day; and 
(2)  For minors age 16 and 17 years, between the hours of 12:00 midnight on any day and 6:00 a.m. of the following day. 
(Code 1996, § 62-121)  
Sec. 36-107. - Exceptions. 
The provisions of section 36-106 shall not apply in the following instances when a minor is: 
(1)  Accompanied by his parent, guardian or other adult person having the lawful care and custody of the minor; 
(2)  Upon an emergency errand directed by his parent or guardian or other adult person having the lawful care and custody of a minor; 
(3)  Returning directly home, by the most direct and efficient route, from a school activity, entertainment, recreational activity or dance; 
(4)  Returning directly home, by the most direct and efficient route, from lawful employment that makes it necessary to be in the places described in section 36-106 during the prescribed period of time; 
(5)  On the sidewalk abutting a minor's residence or abutting the residence of a next door neighbor if the neighbor did not complain to the police officer about such minor's presence; 
(6)  Attending or traveling directly to or from an activity involving the exercise of First Amendment rights of free speech, freedom of assembly or free exercise of religion; and 
(7)  In interstate travel through the city. 
(Code 1996, § 62-122)  
Sec. 36-108. - Parental responsibility. 
Except in circumstances set out in section 36-107, it shall be unlawful for the parent, guardian or other adult person having the care and custody of a minor under the age of 18 years to permit, whether knowingly or through ineffective control or supervision, such minor to loiter, idle, wander, stroll or play in or upon the public streets, highways, roads, alleys, parks, playgrounds or other public grounds, public places or public buildings, places of amusement or entertainment, eating places, vacant lots or any other places normally accessible to the general public for public use, whether on foot or in a motor vehicle or by any other means, during the following periods of time: 
(1)  For minors age 15 years and under, between the hours of 10:30 p.m. on any day and 6:00 a.m. of the following day; and 
(2)  For minors age 16 and 17 years, between the hours of 12:00 midnight on any day and 6:00 a.m. of the following day. 
(Code 1996, § 62-123)  
Sec. 36-109. - Notice of violation. 
Any minor violating the provisions of this article shall be dealt with in accordance with juvenile court law and procedure. Any police officer finding a minor under the age of 18 years violating the provisions of this article shall warn the minor to desist from such violation and to immediately return home and shall cause a written notice to be served upon the parent, guardian or person in charge of a minor, setting forth the manner in which the provisions of this article have been violated. For the purposes of this article, notice shall be deemed properly served upon the parent, guardian or person in charge of a minor if a copy of the notice is served upon him personally or if a copy is sent by certified mail with return receipt requested, to his last known address. 
(Code 1996, § 62-124)  
Sec. 36-110. - Penalty for violation of article. 
Any parent, guardian, or person having the care and custody of a minor who shall permit, whether knowingly or through ineffective control or supervision, a minor to violate the provisions of this article, after receiving written notice that such minor has previously violated this article, shall be subject to a mandatory fine of not less than $50.00 nor more than $500.00, plus costs, for the first such offense, and for each and every subsequent conviction for a violation of this article involving the same minor, the mandatory minimum fine shall be in an amount $100.00 greater than the previous fine imposed. 
(Code 1996, § 62-125)  
Chapter 38 - PLANNING  
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Secs. 38-1—38-18. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - DOWNTOWN DEVELOPMENT AUTHORITY[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Downtown Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-42-1 et seq. 
 
Sec. 38-19. - Declaration of need. 
There is hereby determined and declared a pressing, existing and future need for a downtown development authority to function in the city for the purpose of developing and promoting for the public good and general welfare, trade, commerce, industry and employment opportunities in that geographic area shown on a map thereof on file in the office of the city clerk, called the downtown development area, as that term is defined in the Downtown Development Authorities Law. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-1; Code 1996, § 66-31)  
Sec. 38-20. - Activation. 
There is hereby activated in the city the public body corporate and politic known as the downtown development authority, which authority shall be comprised, authorized and shall act pursuant to the Downtown Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-42-1 et seq. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-2; Code 1996, § 66-32)  
Sec. 38-21. - Directors. 
Each of the persons named as initial directors of the downtown development authority shall serve in such capacity for the number of years designated by the mayor and council, and if at the end of any term of office of any director, a successor therein shall not have been elected, then the director whose term of office shall have expired shall continue to hold office until his successor shall be so elected. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-3; Code 1996, § 66-33)  
Sec. 38-22. - Powers and duties; organization. 
The board of directors shall organize itself, carry out its duties and responsibilities and exercise its powers and prerogatives in accordance with the terms and provisions of the Downtown Development Authorities Law as it now exists and as it might hereafter be amended or modified. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-4; Code 1996, § 66-34)  
Secs. 38-23—38-47. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - PLANNING COMMISSION 
 
Sec. 38-48. - Created. 
In order to guide and accomplish a coordinated and harmonious development of the city which will, in accordance with existing and future needs, best promote the public health, safety, morals, order, convenience, prosperity, and the general welfare, as well as efficiency and economy in the process of development, the city planning commission, referred to in this article as the planning commission, is hereby created and established, and the commission shall be organized and empowered as set forth in this article. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-11; Code 1996, § 66-61)  
Sec. 38-49. - Composition; appointment and term of members. 
The planning commission shall consist of five members, who shall be residents of the city and who shall be appointed by the mayor and council. The terms of the members shall be for four years. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-12; Code 1996, § 66-62)  
Sec. 38-50. - Filling of vacancies; removal of members. 
Any vacancy in membership on the planning commission shall be filled for the unexpired term by the mayor and council, who shall also have the authority to remove any member for cause, on written charges, after a public hearing. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-13; Code 1996, § 66-63)  
Sec. 38-51. - Compensation of members; reimbursement for expenses. 
All members of the planning commission shall serve without compensation but may be reimbursed for actual expenses incurred in connection with their official duties. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-14; Code 1996, § 66-64)  
Sec. 38-52. - Election and term of chairperson. 
The planning commission shall elect its chairperson from among its members. The term of the chairperson shall be one year with eligibility for re-election. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-15; Code 1996, § 66-65)  
Sec. 38-53. - Appointment of secretary. 
The planning commission shall appoint a secretary, who may be an officer or employee of the city. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-16; Code 1996, § 66-66)  
Sec. 38-54. - Rules of procedure; times of meetings. 
The planning commission shall make its own rules of procedure and determine its times of meeting. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-17; Code 1996, § 66-67)  
Sec. 38-55. - Powers and duties. 
(a)  It shall be the function and duty of the planning commission to make such careful and comprehensive surveys and studies of existing conditions and probable future developments and to prepare such plans for physical, social and economic growth as will best promote the public health, safety, morals, convenience, prosperity or the general welfare as well as efficiency and economy in the development of its political jurisdiction. In particular, the planning commission shall have the power and duty to: 
(1)  Prepare a master plan or parts of such plan for the development of the city. 
(2)  Prepare and recommend for adoption to the mayor and council a zoning ordinance or resolution and map for the city. 
(3)  Prepare and recommend for adoption to the mayor and council regulations for the subdivision of land within the city, and to administer the subdivision regulations that may be adopted. 
(4)  Prepare and recommend for adoption to the mayor and council, plats or an official map showing the exact location of the boundary lines of existing, proposed, extended, widened or narrowed streets, and public open spaces or public building sites, together with regulations to control the erection of buildings or other structures within such lines, within its political jurisdiction or a specified portion thereof. 
(b)  The planning commission may make, publish and distribute maps, plans and reports and recommendations relating to the plan and development of the city to public officials and agencies, public utility companies, civic, educational, professional and other organizations and citizens. It may recommend to the executive or legislative officials of the city programs for public improvements and the financing thereof. All public officials shall, upon request, furnish to the planning commission, within a reasonable time, such available information as it may require for its work. The planning commission, its members and employees, in the performance of its functions, may enter upon any land, make examinations and surveys, and place and maintain necessary monuments and marks; provided, however, that the planning commission shall be liable for any injury or damage to property resulting therefrom. In general, the planning commission shall have such powers as may be necessary to enable it to perform its functions and promote the planning of its political jurisdiction. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-18; Code 1996, § 66-68)  
Sec. 38-56. - Expenditures. 
The expenditures of the planning commission, exclusive of gifts, shall be within amounts appropriated for the purpose by the mayor and council. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-19; Code 1996, § 66-69)  
Sec. 38-57. - Employees and staff; contracts for services. 
The planning commission may appoint such employees and staff as it may deem necessary for its work and may contract with the state planning agency and city planners and other consultants for such services as it may require. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-20; Code 1996, § 66-70)  
Sec. 38-58. - Meetings at which official action taken open to public. 
All meetings of the planning commission at which official action is taken shall be open to the public. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-21; Code 1996, § 66-71)  
Sec. 38-59. - Records to be public. 
The records of the planning commission shall be a public record. 
(Code 1984, § 8-1-22; Code 1996, § 66-72)  
Chapter 40 - SOLID WASTE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Georgia Comprehensive Solid Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-20 et seq. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 40-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Construction and demolition waste (C&D waste) means waste building material and rubble resulting from construction, remodeling, repair, and demolition operations on pavements, houses, commercial buildings, and other structures. Such wastes include, but are not limited to, wood, brick, metal, concrete, wall board, paper, cardboard, inert waste, landfill material, and other nonputrescible wastes which have a low potential for groundwater contamination. 
Household garbage (HHG) or garbage means all waste accumulations of animal, fruit or vegetable matter that result from the preparation, use, cooking of or dealing in the storage of meat, fish, fowl, fruits, vegetables or other foods and shall include the containers and wrappings used for the storage of all such substances. The term "household garbage" or "garbage" may also include such other items as are normally used and disposed of by a residence or business, in accordance with the state rules of solid waste management, Ga. Comp. Rules and Regs. ch. 391-3-4. 
Residence or residential unit means any premises occupied and used by a person as a separate household or living quarters. 
Rubbish means all disposable matter other than that included within the terms "construction and demolition waste," "household garbage," "garbage," "tires," and "yard waste" or "organic yard waste." 
Tires or old tires means rubber or synthetic rubber pneumatic tires which have been removed from passenger and commercial vehicles, motorized bikes, trailers, tractors and farm implements, and other utility conveyances which have been worn or damaged to a point where they are of no continued use for the purpose for which they were originally intended. 
Yard waste or organic yard waste means leaves, brush, grass, clippings, shrub and tree prunings, discarded Christmas trees, nursery and greenhouse vegetative residuals and vegetative matter resulting from landscape maintenance other than commercial, agricultural, mining or silvicultural operations. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-1; Code 1996, § 70-1)  
Secs. 40-2—40-20. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL 
 
Sec. 40-21. - Applicability of article. 
The provisions of this article shall apply separately to each residential or commercial unit of the city. 
(Code 1996, § 70-31)  
Sec. 40-22. - Penalty for violation of article. 
In addition to other penalties provided by this Code, the sanitation department of the city or the city's duly approved and licensed independent contractors shall decline to render sanitation services to the residential unit of such person until the residential unit is in complete compliance with the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1996, § 70-32)  
Sec. 40-23. - Containers. 
The occupants of each residential, commercial, or other unit shall utilize the garbage container furnished by the city or the city's duly approved and licensed independent garbage collection contractor. Each user shall be responsible for the safekeeping of the container, and upon its disappearance, shall be required to replace the same at the expense of the residential, commercial, or other user. It shall be unlawful for any person to set fire to the contents of, indiscriminately scatter, disperse the contents of, or otherwise vandalize any container provided either by the city or by a property owner for the dumping of household garbage or other waste materials. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-3; Code 1996, § 70-33)  
Sec. 40-24. - Prerequisite for collection. 
The sanitation department of the city, or the city's duly approved and licensed independent contractor, shall not collect any household garbage unless the garbage is stored in a proper container as described in this article and shall not collect any rubbish or yard waste unless the rubbish or yard waste is deposited as described in this article. 
(Code 1996, § 70-34)  
Sec. 40-25. - Garbage, trash and refuse; accumulation. 
No person who shall own or occupy premises within the city shall permit trash, garbage to accumulate, collect or remain on such premises, except during periods between city sanitation department pickups. No person who shall own or occupy premises where collection is required shall refuse collection or otherwise fail to comply with the requirements of this article. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-7; Code 1996, § 70-35)  
Sec. 40-26. - Garbage, trash and refuse; scattering. 
No person who shall own or occupy premises in the city shall permit garbage, trash or refuse to be scattered from such premises into the public streets or alleys of the city. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-8; Code 1996, § 70-36)  
Sec. 40-27. - Placement of containers for collection. 
All household garbage roll-out containers shall be placed at curbside by 8:00 a.m. on the day of the week selected as pickup day for a particular address, and removed from the curb after collection on that same day. No garbage, debris, garbage containers, or other material shall be placed so that it creates an obstruction of the streets and/or sidewalks within the city. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-4; Code 1996, § 70-37)  
Sec. 40-28. - Classification of premises. 
Each business and commercial premises within the city shall be assigned a commercial classification by the city based on the average number of cubic yards of garbage, trash and refuse collected from such premises within the three preceding months. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-11; Code 1996, § 70-38)  
Sec. 40-29. - Collection schedule. 
Garbage, trash, and refuse shall be collected from the various premises in the city by the proper department of the city as follows: 
(1)  Collections from residential units shall be made not less than once weekly. 
(2)  Collections from businesses or commercial premises shall be made not less than once weekly or in conformity with such schedule as established from time to time by the mayor and council for specific businesses. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-12; Code 1996, § 70-39)  
Sec. 40-30. - Sanitary charge assessed. 
A monthly sanitary charge, as established by the mayor and council, is hereby assessed against the owner or occupant of every improved premises within the city for which the occupant shall be liable for payment. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-13; Code 1996, § 70-40)  
Sec. 40-31. - Sanitary charge billing. 
(a)  The monthly sanitary charge for each premises to which the city supplies water service shall be billed and collected in the same manner and at the same time as water or sewer service is billed and collected. 
(b)  The monthly sanitary charge for each premises to which the city does not supply water or sewer service shall be billed and collected monthly in advance by the tenth day of each month and shall be payable by the occupant or owner at the city clerk's office at the city hall. 
(c)  In all instances when a residential unit is occupied by more than one single-family unit and is served by a single water meter, the sanitary charges applicable to the residential premises at such location shall all be billed to the person in whose name the water meter is registered at the office of the city clerk, the sanitary charge to be included thereon for each family unit on the premises. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-14; Code 1996, § 70-41)  
Sec. 40-32. - Sanitary charge; effect of failure to pay. 
(a)  Execution, levy and sale authorized. Should any person liable for payment of the sanitary charges hereby imposed fail to pay the same within ten days after having been billed therefor, the city clerk is authorized to issue an execution therefor against such person and shall deliver such execution to the city marshal for a levy and sale as provided by law. 
(b)  Discontinuance of city services. Any person failing for any reason or refusing to pay the monthly sanitary charge provided for in this article after having been duly billed for such charge by the city shall be deemed guilty of a violation of this article, and all sanitary services and water services provided by the city to the premises for which the monthly charges are past due shall be terminated by the city in accordance with the provisions for termination of water service. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-15; Code 1996, § 70-42)  
Sec. 40-33. - Recycling newspapers; other paper waste. 
Residents are encouraged to recycle newspapers and all other acceptable paper waste by placing same in the drop-off facilities designated within the city. More than seven days' accumulation of newspapers, or more than five volumes of magazines or other printed matter, shall not be collected unless securely fastened in bundles weighing not more than 50 pounds and deposited at curbside. 
(Code 1996, § 70-43)  
Sec. 40-34. - Recycling cardboard; commercial establishments. 
All commercial business establishments and other producers of significant numbers, or amounts of cardboard boxes or other cardboard or corrugated materials, shall separate and collect all clean unwaxed cardboard wastes and deposit such material in a designated bin or container so that the material can be picked up by the city's sanitation department, or duly authorized and approved independent contractor, for recycling and reuse. 
(Code 1996, § 70-44)  
Sec. 40-35. - Recycling cardboard; residential households. 
Residential households are encouraged to recycle cardboard and other corrugated materials by depositing same into a commercial business's bin, or by depositing the material in the cardboard recycling bin at the city utility department's maintenance complex. 
(Code 1996, § 70-45)  
Sec. 40-36. - Rubbish. 
Rubbish shall be collected by the city sanitation department, provided the accumulation thereof is not in violation of any other section of this article, and provided the rubbish is separated in piles according to type and category as may be established by rules promulgated by the city sanitation department from time to time, or by the mayor and council of the city. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-6; Code 1996, § 70-46)  
Sec. 40-37. - Construction and demolition waste. 
Construction and demolition waste, such as lumber, plaster, roofing, concrete, bricks, blocks, or similar materials resulting from construction, repair, demolition, or improvement of buildings, is the responsibility of the property owner or contractor and will not be removed by the city sanitation department. It shall be unlawful for the owner of such waste materials, or any other person, to place such materials on the streets, sidewalks, or rights-of-way of the city. 
(Code 1984, § 5-2-6; Code 1996, § 70-47)  
Sec. 40-38. - Dirt, rocks and stumps. 
Dirt, rocks and stumps will not be removed by the city, and it shall be unlawful for the owner of such materials, or any other person, to place such materials on the streets or sidewalks of the city. 
(Code 1996, § 70-48)  
Sec. 40-39. - Appliances and furniture. 
Appliances and furniture, such as refrigerators, water heaters, stoves, sinks, televisions, chairs, couches and the like, exceeding 75 pounds in weight, shall not be collected by the city sanitation department. It shall be unlawful for the owner or any other person to cause such items to be placed upon the streets, sidewalks or rights-of-way of the city. 
(Code 1996, § 70-49)  
Sec. 40-40. - Trees and parts of trees; shrubbery clippings; other matter. 
(a)  Trees, parts of trees, shrubbery clippings or any like matter exceeding six inches in diameter or six feet in length shall not be collected by the city sanitation department. It shall be unlawful for the owner, or any other person, to cause such materials to be placed upon the streets, sidewalks or rights-of-way of the city. 
(b)  Trees, parts of trees, shrubbery clippings or any like matter not exceeding six inches in diameter and not exceeding six feet in length, lawn clippings and other organic yard waste generated by normal yard maintenance by the resident or property owner will be collected, provided the same is placed at curbside in a separate pile not containing any other class of waste, and provided the amount put out at any one time does not exceed one-half of a truckload. Any amount deposited at curbside in excess of one-half of a truckload will be removed by the sanitation department upon the special request of the property owner, for a fee, as established by the mayor and council, for each load or partial truckload. 
(c)  Whenever the organic waste mentioned in subsection (b) of this section is generated by a commercial contractor or any individual who is providing his services for pay or gain in any fashion, it shall be the responsibility of the property owner or contractor or person providing his services for pay or gain to collect and properly dispose of any organic waste produced in the accomplishment of the task for which his services have been engaged. 
(Code 1996, § 70-50) 
State Law reference— Yard trimmings disposal restrictions, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-40.2.  
Sec. 40-41. - Materials not to be deposited. 
It shall be unlawful to place in any garbage or rubbish container any acid, or other dangerous liquids, or other nonhazardous liquids in containers of more than one gallon, or any substance which is prohibited or which could cause injury to the persons engaged in removing such containers. 
(Code 1996, § 70-51)  
Sec. 40-42. - Tires. 
(a)  Tires are the responsibility of the owner; the city sanitation department will not collect and dispose of them. It shall be unlawful for the owner thereof, or any other person, to cause the same to be placed upon the streets, sidewalks, or rights-of-way of the city, or upon the property of another person. Tires shall not be allowed to collect or accumulate out from under permanent cover upon the property of any owner in such manner that, in the judgment of the chief of police, the accumulation thereof may be a menace to public health, either by creating a refuge for vermin, rodents, snakes or other varmints, or as a breeding place for mosquitoes or other similar insects. 
(b)  Unless otherwise provided by law, the violation of this section shall be punished by a fine in the amount of $50.00 for the first improperly disposed of tire, and $100.00 each for each additional improperly disposed of tire up to a maximum penalty provided by law. 
(Code 1996, § 70-52; Ord. of 3-2-2009, § 70-52)  
Secs. 40-43—40-72. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - LITTER CONTROL[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Litter Control Law, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-40 et seq.; littering highways, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-249. 
 
Sec. 40-73. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Litter means all discarded sand, gravel, slag, brickbats, rubbish, waste material, tin or aluminum cans, refuse, garbage, trash, debris, dead animals, or other discarded materials of every kind and description. 
Public or private property means the right-of-way of any road or highway; any body of water or watercourse or the shores thereof; any park, playground, building, refuge, or conservation or recreation area; and any vacant areas, commercial, industrial, residential or farm properties, timberlands, or forests. 
(Code 1996, § 70-76)  
Sec. 40-74. - Dumping or depositing of litter. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to dump, deposit, throw, leave or to cause or permit the dumping, depositing, placing, throwing or leaving of litter on any public or private property in this city, or any waters in this city, unless the litter is discarded in accordance with the requirements of this article, or otherwise placed into a litter receptacle or container installed or placed on such property and specifically designated for the use of the general public. The provisions of this subsection shall not be read or construed to prohibit the owner or renter of any private property, nor any person acting with the consent of such owner or renter, from dumping, depositing, placing, throwing, or leaving of litter in any private receptacle or container maintained by the owner or renter of such private property for the sole and exclusive use of the household or business of such owner or renter. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to dump, deposit, throw or leave, or to cause or permit the dumping, depositing, placing, throwing or leaving of litter on any private property in this city, in any litter receptacle thereon, or any waters in this city, unless the person is the owner or tenant in lawful possession of such property or such person has first obtained the consent of the owner or tenant in such lawful possession. 
(Code 1996, § 70-78)  
Sec. 40-75. - Prima facie evidence; rebuttable presumption. 
(a)  Whenever litter is thrown, deposited, dropped or dumped from any motor vehicle, boat, airplane or other conveyance in violation of section 40-74, it shall be prima facie evidence that the operator of the conveyance has violated this article. 
(b)  Except as provided in subsection (a) of this section, whenever any litter which is dumped, deposited, thrown, or left on public or private property in violation of section 40-74 is discovered to contain any articles, including, but not limited to, letters, bills, publications, or other writings, which display the name of a person thereon in such a manner as to indicate that the articles belong or belonged to such person, it shall be a rebuttable presumption that such person has violated section 40-74. 
(Code 1996, § 70-79)  
Chapter 42 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Obstructing sidewalks or other public passages, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-43; regulation of maintenance and use of public roads generally, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-1 et seq.; grant by municipal corporation of right to obstruct public street prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 36-30-10; power to construct and maintain roads, including curbs, sidewalks, streetlights and devices to control the flow of traffic, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(4). 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 42-1. - Moving buildings. 
(a)  Permit required. It shall be unlawful for any person to move a building or structure on, over, across or through the public streets and places of the city without first obtaining a permit from the mayor and council. 
(b)  Permit fee. The fee for a permit required by subsection (a) of this section shall be as fixed from time to time by the mayor and council. 
(c)  Bond required. Any person desiring to move a building or structure on, over, across or through the public streets and places of the city shall post a bond with the city clerk in the amount of $5,000.00, payable to the city. 
(d)  Insurance required. Any person desiring to move a building or structure on, over, across or through the public streets and places of the city shall provide proof that he is currently insured for general liability coverage applicable to any damages he might cause in moving the building or structure in an amount of not less than $100,000.00. 
(Code 1984, § 5-1-1; Code 1996, § 74-1)  
Sec. 42-2. - Goods, wares and merchandise obstructing sidewalks. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep any goods, wares or merchandise of any kind or description, including stoves, refrigerators and furniture, on the sidewalk of the city so as to hinder or obstruct the use of such sidewalks. In no event shall such merchandise extend more than two feet from the building. 
(Code 1984, § 5-1-2; Code 1996, § 74-2)  
Sec. 42-3. - Parking for sale of wares and merchandise from vehicles. 
There shall not be conducted from any truck, motor vehicle, wagon, trailer or other similar type of conveyance, any merchandise business on the streets of the city within a business district, except with special permission in writing from the mayor and council. 
(Code 1984, § 5-1-3; Code 1996, § 74-3)  
Sec. 42-4. - Using streets and sidewalks to repair or store vehicles. 
It shall be unlawful for any person operating and maintaining a garage in the city for the purpose of repairing or storing motor vehicles to use any of the streets, alleys or sidewalks for the purpose of parking those motor vehicles or for the purpose of washing, painting or repairing them. 
(Code 1984, § 5-1-4; Code 1996, § 74-4)  
Sec. 42-5. - Glass and other dangerous or unsightly material on streets. 
(a)  No person shall throw or deposit upon any street any glass bottle, glass, nails, tacks, wire, cans, rubbish, garbage, trash or other dangerous or unsightly material which is likely to injure any person, animal or vehicle upon such street. 
(b)  Any person who drops, or permits to be dropped or thrown, upon any street any destructive or injurious material shall immediately remove the material or cause it to be removed. 
(c)  Any person removing a wrecked or damaged vehicle from a street shall remove any glass or other injurious substance dropped upon the street from such vehicle. 
(Code 1984, § 5-1-5; Code 1996, § 74-5)  
Sec. 42-6. - Installations and alterations to right-of-way; permit and deposit required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to make any alterations, including, but not limited to, damage or removal or pavement or installations of any kind, within the right-of-way or on the streets and sidewalks of the city for any purpose whatever without applying to and obtaining written permission from the city manager. The city manager may require that such person make a deposit of such sum of money as may be determined from time to time by the mayor and council in order to ensure that such street or sidewalk shall be restored. Such sum of money shall be returned to such person only upon proper restoration of the street or sidewalk. 
(Code 1984, § 5-1-6; Code 1996, § 74-6)  
Secs. 42-7—42-30. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - PARADES 
 
Sec. 42-31. - Permit required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to participate in, conduct or accompany any organized parade or procession, other than a funeral procession, on the public streets, sidewalks or other public property in the city unless an application has been filed at least 30 days prior to the proposed date of such parade or procession and a permit granted to conduct such parade, picket or procession within the city. 
(Code 1984, § 5-1-21; Code 1996, § 74-31)  
Sec. 42-32. - Application for parade permit. 
(a)  An application for permit to conduct or sponsor a parade or procession shall be filed with the city clerk in writing and shall contain the following information furnished by the person in official charge of the proposed parade, picket or procession: 
(1)  The name of all organizations or persons organizing or sponsoring the parade or procession. 
(2)  The purpose of the parade or procession. 
(3)  The date and hours of the parade or procession. 
(4)  The proposed route of the parade or procession, and its beginning and termination points. 
(5)  The number and types of vehicles, marching units and floats to be used in the parade or procession. 
(6)  The number of persons participating in the parade or procession. 
(b)  For all parades and processions, the route of which will move along or cross state roads, written clearance from the state department of transportation must accompany the permit application. 
(Code 1984, § 5-1-22; Code 1996, § 74-32)  
Sec. 42-33. - Investigation of applicant.
