ARTICLE IV. - TRUCK ROUTES 
 
Sec. 48-99. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Truck means all utility motor vehicles, which together with load, weigh in excess of 8,000 pounds and which are designed for the purpose of transporting materials, goods, freight, liquids, farm products, machinery, or other items upon the streets or roads of the city. 
(Code 1996, § 86-96)  
Sec. 48-100. - Designation of streets and parts of streets on which truck traffic is prohibited; signs required. 
When appropriate signs are erected giving notice, all trucks are hereby prohibited upon the streets or parts of streets so designated; however, such restriction shall not apply to trucks making local deliveries within the areas so posted when proper documentation is provided to verify such delivery. 
(Code 1996, § 86-97)  
Sec. 48-101. - Truck routes designated; use regulated. 
(a)  Truck routes within the city are hereby designated as follows: 
(1)  All state department of transportation (DOT) routes or federal highway system routes. 
(2)  Broome Avenue, from W. Third Street (GA 38 - US 84) to W. Crawford Street (GA 39 North). 
(3)  Crawford Street, from N. Tennille Ave. (GA 91) to Eastgate Avenue. 
(4)  Friendship Avenue, from E. Third Street (GA 38 - US 84) to Crawford Street. 
(b)  All trucks other than trucks making local deliveries within the city shall use the streets designated in this section and no others. 
(Code 1996, § 86-98)  
Sec. 48-102. - Vehicles weighing more than 8,000 pounds; authorized routes through city designated. 
All motor vehicles which, together with load, weigh in excess of 8,000 pounds, passing through, entering or leaving the city shall be restricted to such streets and parts of streets designated for such traffic by the mayor and council from time to time, subject to the exceptions set out in section 48-104. 
(Code 1996, § 86-99)  
Sec. 48-103. - Parking trucks in residential areas. 
(a)  All other provisions of this Code notwithstanding, it shall be unlawful for any person to stop or park a tractor, trailer or semitrailer upon any public street in the city in a residential area. 
(b)  For the purpose of this section, the term "residential area" shall mean any area within the city which is zoned R-A or R-B. 
(c)  For the purpose of this section, the term "trailer" or "semitrailer" shall mean a vehicle with or without motive power, other than a pole trailer, designed for carrying persons or property, and for being drawn by a motor vehicle and so constructed that some of the weight and that of its load rests upon or is carried by another vehicle. 
(d)  For the purpose of this section, the term "tractor" shall mean a motor vehicle designed for and principally used for the pulling and movement of trailers and semitrailers. 
(Ord. of 3-6-2007, § 86-99(a))  
Sec. 48-104. - Vehicles weighing more than 8,000 pounds; duties of operator; exceptions. 
Each motor vehicle, falling within the provisions of section 48-101, entering the city by any other road or street than those set out in section 48-101 shall proceed by the shortest route to the nearest street or part of a street set out in section 48-101 and shall proceed thence along the streets or parts of streets named through the city, subject to the following exceptions: 
(1)  Vehicles based within city. Motor vehicles having a base within the corporate limits may proceed to such base by the shortest route from the streets and parts of streets set out in section 48-101 and shall likewise return to such streets or parts of streets by the shortest route. 
(2)  Servicing vehicle. Motor vehicles may leave the streets and parts of streets set out in section 48-101 for the purpose of purchasing fuel and oil or securing repairs, but in such case they shall be permitted only upon such streets and parts of streets as are upon the most direct and shortest route from the streets and parts of streets set out in section 48-101. 
(3)  Loading and unloading. Motor vehicles may leave the streets and parts of streets set out in section 48-101 for the purpose of making deliveries consigned to points upon other streets, roads and alleys in the city and for the further purpose of receiving goods or other property for transportation from points upon other roads, streets and alleys within the corporate limits, but shall proceed to such points by the shortest direct route from the streets and parts of streets set out in section 48-101 and shall return by the same route. 
(Code 1996, § 86-100)  
Chapter 50 - UTILITIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Authority to acquire, construct, extend, operate, maintain and collect fees for water and sewerage systems, O.C.G.A. § 36-34-5. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 50-1. - Destruction or damage to utility apparatus; diversion of services. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person intentionally and without authority to destroy, damage or tamper with any meter, pipe, conduit, wire, line, post, lamp or other apparatus owned by the city or by any company engaged in the manufacture, distribution, or sale of electricity, gas, water, telephone, cable television or other public service. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person intentionally and without authority to prevent a meter from properly registering the quantity of such service supplied, or in any way to interfere with the proper action of the city, or of a company engaged in the manufacture, distribution, or sale of electricity, gas, water, telephone, cable television or other public service, or intentionally to divert any of the services of the city, or such company, or otherwise intentionally and without authority to use or cause to be used, without the consent of the city or such company, any service manufactured, sold or distributed by the city or such company. 
(c)  No person shall knowingly receive the benefit of acts of diversion of, or tampering with, electricity, gas, water, telephone, cable television or other public service without the proper charge. 
(d)  Proof that any of the acts specified in this section was done on premises in possession of an accused, or that the accused received the benefit of any such act, shall be prima facie evidence that the accused committed such act or aided and abetted in the commission of such act. 
(Code 1984, § 6-1-1; Code 1996, § 90-1)  
Sec. 50-2. - Mandatory use of city's water system. 
No water service, aside from that provided through the city, may be constructed, reconstructed, maintained or otherwise established within the city so long as connection to the city water system is available. 
(Ord. No. 05-07-19, 6-4-2019)  
Sec. 50-3. - Water and sewer rates and charges. 
Water and sewer rates and charges shall be as established by the mayor and council. Failure to pay such rates and charges shall constitute a lien upon the property to which water and sewer service is rendered by the city. 
(Code 1984, § 6-1-2; Code 1996, § 90-2)  
Sec. 50-4. - Resale of water. 
The resale of water purchased from the city is expressly prohibited. 
(Code 1984, § 6-1-3; Code 1996, § 90-3)  
Secs. 50-5—50-24. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - WATER CONSERVATION 
 
Sec. 50-25. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Commercial means any type of building other than residential. 
Construction means the erection of a new building or the alteration of an existing building in connection with its repair or renovation or in connection with making an addition to an existing building and shall include the replacement of a malfunctioning, unserviceable, or obsolete faucet, showerhead, toilet or urinal in an existing building. 
Residential means any building or unit of a building intended for occupancy as a dwelling, but shall not include a hotel or motel. 
(Code 1996, § 90-31; Ord. of 1-8-1991, § 1)  
Sec. 50-26. - Enforcement of article. 
This article shall be enforced by the office of the city building official. Citations for violations may be issued by the city building official. 
(Code 1996, § 90-32; Ord. of 1-8-1991, § 6(a))  
Sec. 50-27. - Prohibited plumbing fixtures. 
No construction may be initiated within the city for any residential building of any type which employs a: 
(1)  Gravity tank-type, flushometer valve, or flushometer tank toilet that uses more than an average of 1? gallons of water per flush; 
(2)  Showerhead that allows a flow of more than an average of 2½ gallons of water per minute at 60 pounds per square inch of pressure; 
(3)  Urinal that uses more than an average of one gallon of water per flush; 
(4)  Lavatory faucet or lavatory replacement aerator that allows a flow of more than two gallons of water per minute; or 
(5)  Kitchen faucet or kitchen replacement aerator that allows a flow of more than 2½ gallons of water per minute. 
(Code 1996, § 90-34; Ord. of 1-8-1991, § 1)  
Sec. 50-28. - Application of section 50-27 to residential and commercial construction. 
The requirements of section 50-27 shall apply to any residential construction and to any commercial construction which involves the repair or renovation of or addition to any existing building when such repair or renovation of or addition to such existing building includes replacement of toilets or showers, or both. 
(Code 1996, § 90-36; Ord. of 1-8-1991, § 4)  
Sec. 50-29. - Exemptions. 
(a)  New construction and the repair or renovation of an existing building shall be exempt from the requirements of this article when: 
(1)  The repair or renovation of the existing building does not include the replacement of the plumbing or sewage system servicing toilets, faucets or showerheads within such existing buildings; 
(2)  Such plumbing or sewage system within such existing building, because of its capacity, design or installation, would not function properly if the toilets, faucets or showerheads required by this article were installed; 
(3)  Such system is a well or gravity flow from a spring and is owned privately by an individual for use in such individual's personal residence; or 
(4)  Units to be installed are: 
a.  Specifically designed for use by the handicapped; 
b.  Specifically designed to withstand unusual abuse or installation in a penal institution; or 
c.  Toilets for juveniles. 
(b)  The owner or his agent of a building undergoing new construction, repair or renovation who is entitled to an exemption as specified in subsection (a)(2), (a)(3) or (a)(4) of this section shall obtain the exemption by applying at the office of the city building official. A fee, as established by the mayor and council, shall be charged for the inspection and issuance of such exemption. 
(Code 1996, § 90-37; Ord. of 1-8-1991, § 5)  
Sec. 50-30. - Restriction on outdoor watering of landscape. 
Outdoor watering for purposes of planting, growing, managing, or maintaining ground cover, trees, shrubs, or other plants may occur only between the hours of 4:00 p.m. and 10:00 a.m.; provided, however, that this limitation shall not create any limitation upon the following outdoor water uses: 
(1)  Commercial raising, harvesting, or storing of crops; feeding, breeding, or managing livestock or poultry; commercial production or storing of feed for use in the production of livestock, including, but not limited to, cattle, calves, swine, hogs, goats, sheep, and rabbits, or for use in the production of poultry, including, but not limited to, chickens, hens, ratites, and turkeys; producing plants, trees, fowl, or animals; or commercial production of aquacultural, horticultural, dairy, livestock, poultry, eggs, and apiarian products or as otherwise defined in O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3; 
(2)  Capture and reuse of cooling system condensate or stormwater in compliance with applicable city ordinances and state guidelines; 
(3)  Reuse of gray water in compliance with O.C.G.A. § 31-3-5.2 and applicable local board of health regulations; 
(4)  Use of reclaimed waste water by a designated user from a system permitted by the environmental protection division of the state department of natural resources to provide reclaimed waste water; 
(5)  Watering personal food gardens; 
(6)  Watering new and replanted plant, seed, or turf in landscapes, golf courses, or sports turf fields during installation and for a period of 30 days immediately following the date of installation; 
(7)  Drip irrigation or irrigation using soaker hoses; 
(8)  Hand watering with a hose with automatic cutoff or handheld container; 
(9)  Use of water withdrawn from private water wells or surface water by an owner or operator of property if such well or surface water is on said property; 
(10)  Watering horticultural crops held for sale, resale, or installation; 
(11)  Watering athletic fields, golf courses, or public turf grass recreational areas; 
(12)  Installation, maintenance, or calibration of irrigation systems; or 
(13)  Hydroseeding. 
(Ord. of 11-2-2010, § 90-38)  
Sec. 50-31. - Enforcement. 
The chief of police shall be the enforcement authority for this article. The county/city manager may also authorize other departments as may be deemed necessary to support enforcement. 
(Ord. of 11-2-2010, § 90-39)  
Secs. 50-32—50-50. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - SEWER USE  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 50-51. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Biochemical oxygen demand (BOD) means the calculated pounds of oxygen required to satisfy the five-day oxygen demand of 1,000,000 pounds of waste when tested in accordance with the procedure given in the latest edition of Standard Methods, published by the American Public Health Association. 
Building sewer means that part of the horizontal piping of a building drainage system extending from the outside of the building or end of the inside plumbing system to, and including, the connection with the city sewer system. 
City sewer system means such system composed of sanitary sewers, storm sewers, combined sewers, and sewage treatment works owned by a city. 
Combined sewer means a sewer intended to receive domestic sewage, treated or weak industrial wastes, surface water and stormwater. 
Domestic sewage means liquid from residences, business buildings or institutions which has a daily average of not more than 400 parts per million of BOD and a like amount of suspended solids. 
Industrial wastes means the liquid wastes resulting from processes employed in industrial establishments. An industrial waste will be considered weak when it contains less than 600 parts per million of BOD and suspended solids with no biologically toxic substances in it. 
pH means a measure of acidity or alkalinity which has a range of zero to 14. 
Sanitary sewer means a sewer intended to receive domestic sewage and treated or weak industrial waste without the admixture of surface water, stormwater, or unpolluted industrial process water. 
Storm sewer means a sewer intended to receive stormwater and surface water, street wash, or drainage and sewage and industrial wastes that have been completely purified. 
Suspended solids means the amount of material in suspension expressed in parts per million as determined by the Gooch crucible method given in the latest edition of Standard Methods, published by the American Public Health Association. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-1; Code 1996, § 90-66)  
Sec. 50-52. - Notice of violation. 
Whenever it is found that any person is violating any of the provisions or requirements set out in this article, a written notice, stating the offense and setting a time limit for the correction, shall be served upon the offender by the chief of police. The offender shall, within the time limit stated in the notice served upon him, forever cease all violations. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-9(a); Code 1996, § 90-67)  
Sec. 50-53. - Unsanitary deposits. 
It shall be unlawful for any owner or lessee to place, deposit, or permit to be deposited, any human excrement, garbage or any other organic waste upon the premises in an unsanitary manner. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-2; Code 1996, § 90-69)  
Sec. 50-54. - Discharge of polluted waters to streams, ditches or other underground water source. 
It shall be unlawful to discharge any untreated domestic sewage, industrial wastes or other polluted waters into any streams or ditches or any abandoned water well, or in any way to discharge sewage or industrial waste directly into underground waters within the area controlled by the city. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-3; Code 1996, § 90-70)  
Sec. 50-55. - Connection required where property within 200 feet of city sewer system. 
It shall be unlawful to construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, cesspool or septic tank intended for, or subject to, receiving organic wastes wherever a connection can be made to the city sewer system within 200 feet of any property. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-4; Code 1996, § 90-71)  
Sec. 50-56. - Connection to be at owner's expense; time within which to connect. 
The owner of all houses, buildings or properties situated within the city, abutting on any streets, alleys or parkways, in which there is now located or may hereafter be located any sewer pipeline of the sanitary sewer system of the city, is hereby required, at his own cost and expense, to install suitable toilet facilities and to connect those houses or buildings erected upon the property directly with the sanitary sewer system within three months after notice to do so. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-5; Code 1996, § 90-72)  
Sec. 50-57. - Connection of properties beyond city limits. 
Any person owning or controlling premises located beyond the corporate limits of the city and desiring to install a plumbing system on the premises and connect the system with the sanitary sewers of the city may do so by complying with the requirements of this article and by paying a monthly sewer rental charge. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-6; Code 1996, § 90-73)  
Sec. 50-58. - Method of disposal where sewer unavailable or connection cannot be made. 
Where city sewers are not available, or where a connection, as determined by the mayor and council, cannot be made, a septic tank or another method of private sewage disposal must be constructed according to the requirements of the state department of natural resources. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-7; Code 1996, § 90-74)  
Sec. 50-59. - City's right of entry. 
Authority is hereby granted to the duly authorized city employees to enter upon all properties to make all necessary inspections, tests, and measurements to ensure complete compliance with all of the regulations of this article. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-8; Code 1996, § 90-75)  
Secs. 50-60—50-76. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - BUILDING SEWERS 
 
Sec. 50-77. - Separate sewers required; exception. 
A separate building sewer is required for each individual building or house, whether constructed as a detached unit or as one or a pair or row, but a single building sewer will be permitted to serve an apartment house or other multiple unit structure or industrial plant whose individual apartments or units are not subject to separate ownership. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-21; Code 1996, § 90-91)  
Sec. 50-78. - Connection to be at owner's expense; permit to connect required. 
Building sewers from the point of entry of the city sewer to the building shall be laid by the owner at his expense, but only after such connections have been authorized by a permit issued by the superintendent of utilities upon the submission of evidence by the owner that the discharge from the building sewer will comply with all of the regulations of this article. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-22; Code 1996, § 90-92)  
Sec. 50-79. - Use of old building sewers and drains. 
Old building sewers and drains may be used in connection with new buildings or new plumbing only when they are approved through issue of a permit as for new construction of building sewers. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-23; Code 1996, § 90-93)  
Sec. 50-80. - Diameter and fall. 
All building sewers shall be not less than six inches in diameter and shall have a fall of not less than one-half inch per foot for six-inch pipe and not less than one-quarter inch per foot for pipe eight inches or over in diameter. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-24; Code 1996, § 90-94)  
Sec. 50-81. - Laying of pipes. 
All pipe shall be laid on a uniform grade and, where possible, on a straight line. Where the building sewer cannot be laid on a straight line, curved pipe shall be used for every deflection from a straight line of more than three inches per foot. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-25; Code 1996, § 90-95)  
Sec. 50-82. - Recommendation where sewer near large tree trunks. 
Where building sewers are within 20 feet of large tree trunks, it is recommended that cast iron pipe with leaded joints be used. All joints must be filled, made smooth and absolutely watertight. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-26; Code 1996, § 90-96)  
Sec. 50-83. - Manner of connecting building sewer to city sewer. 
The connection between the building sewer and the city sewer shall be made at the Y branch provided. If no Y branch was left in the city sewer for the building sewer and the city sewer is not over 12 inches in diameter, a Y branch shall be installed in the city sewer at the desired location by the owner of the building sewer. Where the city sewer is over 12 inches in diameter and where no Y branch was left for the building sewer, a hole may be cut in the city sewer large enough to receive the end of the building sewer and the connection made so that the building sewer enters the city sewer at an angle of 45 degrees. A 45-degree ell can be used to make this connection if the spigot end is cut to fit so that it does not extend past the inside surface of the city sewer. City sewers shall not be tapped below the centerline of the city sewer. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-27; Code 1996, § 90-97)  
Sec. 50-84. - Backfilling. 
In backfilling, the material shall be carefully placed and packed around the pipe to provide a uniform bearing and to keep the pipe in proper position. No stones, bricks or like material shall be used in the backfill until there has been a depth of at least 18 inches of fine earth or gravel placed over the pipe. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-28; Code 1996, § 90-98)  
Sec. 50-85. - Maintenance of barricades and lights. 
Proper barricades and lights must be maintained on the banks of the trenches to guard the public against accidents during construction or connection of the building sewer. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-29; Code 1996, § 90-99)  
Secs. 50-86—50-113. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - DISCHARGE OF DELETERIOUS WASTES 
 
Sec. 50-114. - Prohibited discharges to sanitary sewers. 
No stormwater from pavements, areaways, roofs or other sources shall be admitted to the sanitary sewers which are designed to be used exclusively as carriers of domestic sewage and suitable industrial wastes. The same shall apply to unpolluted process or cooling waters. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-41; Code 1996, § 90-116)  
Sec. 50-115. - Discharge of stormwater. 
Stormwater shall be admitted only to such sewers as are specifically designed as combined sewers or storm sewers. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-42; Code 1996, § 90-117)  
Sec. 50-116. - Discharge of liquids and gases above certain temperatures. 
No person shall discharge into any sewer any liquid or gas having a temperature greater than 100 degrees Fahrenheit. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-43; Code 1996, § 90-118)  
Sec. 50-117. - Prohibited discharges to public sewers. 
No person shall discharge or deposit any of the following described waste materials into any sanitary, storm or combined sewer: 
(1)  Liquid waste materials which contain more than 100 parts of oil or grease per million parts, determined by weight; 
(2)  Liquid waste material in which the suspended solids exceed 600 parts per million, determined by weight; 
(3)  Any petroleum product or other product which, by reason of its nature or quality, may cause a fire or explosion, or in any way be injurious to persons or to the sewer system; 
(4)  Any industrial waste with a pH of less than 5.5 or greater than 9.0; 
(5)  Any industrial waste with a five-day biochemical oxygen demand of more than 600 parts per million, by weight; 
(6)  Any industrial waste containing any toxic or poisonous substance in a sufficient quantity to interfere with the biologic processes used in the sewage treatment process or that will pass through the sewage treatment plant and harm persons or aquatic life in the receiving stream; 
(7)  Any unshredded garbage, scraps, or vegetables; or 
(8)  Any straw, ashes, cinders, shavings, butchers' offal, rags, feathers or any other material capable of causing obstructions, nuisance, or injury to or interference with the sewer system. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-44; Code 1996, § 90-119)  
Sec. 50-118. - Sampling manholes. 
(a)  Required in certain instances. Every building sewer discharging industrial wastes from any plant or establishment into the city sewer system may be required, at the discretion of the approving authorities, to have a sampling manhole for the purpose of ascertaining the quality and quantity of the waste flowing in the building sewer. 
(b)  Location; construction. The manhole shall be located at a suitable and satisfactory location and it shall be not less than three feet in inside diameter and built in a manner designated by the superintendent of utilities. 
(c)  Cost. The cost of the manhole shall be borne by the applicant, but the manhole shall become the property of the city government. 
(d)  Maintenance. The responsibility for maintaining the manhole in a safe condition shall be assumed and remain with the owner of the property at all times. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-45; Code 1996, § 90-120)  
Sec. 50-119. - Pretreatment of wastes. 
Whenever the industrial wastes do not meet the requirements of this article, or the quantity of biochemical oxygen demand is one-tenth of the total of the entire wastes of the city, the industry will be required to pretreat its waste or enter into a one-year agreement with the city to treat the waste as discharged. 
(Code 1984, § 6-2-46; Code 1996, § 90-121)  
Secs. 50-120—50-136. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - UNDERGROUND UTILITY INSTALLATIONS 
 
Sec. 50-137. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Damage means the substantial weakening of structural or lateral support of an underground utility, penetration or destruction of any protective coating, housing or other protective device of an underground utility, and the partial or complete severance of an underground utility. 
Demolish or demolition means any operation by which a structure or mass of material is wrecked, razed, rendered, moved or removed by means of any tool, equipment or discharge of explosives. 
Excavate or excavation means an operation for the purpose of the movement or removal of earth, rock or other materials in or on the ground by use of mechanized equipment or by discharge of explosives, and including augering, backfilling, digging, drilling, grading, plowing-in pulling-in, ripping, scraping, trenching and tunneling, but not including the tilling of soil for agricultural purposes. 
Mechanized equipment means equipment operated by means of mechanical power, including trenchers, bulldozers, power shovels, augers, backhoes, scrapers, drills, cable and pipe plows and other equipment used for plowing in or pulling in cable or pipe. 
Operator means any city or utility commission who owns or operates a utility. 
Utility means any line, system or facility used for producing, storing, conveying, transmitting or distributing communication, electricity, gas, petroleum, petroleum products, hazardous liquids, water, steam or sewage. 
Working day means every day, except Saturdays, Sundays and national and legal state holidays. 
(Code 1984, § 6-3-1; Code 1996, § 90-141)  
Sec. 50-138. - Excavation and demolition permits; effect. 
A permit issued pursuant to the law authorizing excavation or demolition operations shall not be deemed to relieve a person from the responsibility for complying with the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1984, § 6-3-2; Code 1996, § 90-143)  
Sec. 50-139. - Prohibited acts. 
Except as provided in section 50-142, no person may excavate in a street, highway, public space, or a private easement of an operator, or near the location of a utility installed on the premises of a customer served by such utility, or demolish a building, without having first ascertained, in the manner prescribed in sections 50-140 and 50-141, the location of all underground utilities in the area that would be affected by the proposed excavation or demolition. Each operator shall maintain a list of all underground utilities and plants or maps showing their location. 
(Code 1984, § 6-3-3; Code 1996, § 90-144)  
Sec. 50-140. - Notice of intent. 
(a)  Except as provided in section 50-142, before commencing any excavation or demolition operation designated in section 50-139, each person responsible for such excavation or demolition shall serve written or telephone notice of intent to excavate or demolish at least three but not more than ten full working days to the state utility protection center prior to any such excavation or demolition. 
(b)  The written or telephonic notice required by subsection (a) of this section must contain the name, address and telephone number of the person filing the notice of intent, and, if different, the person responsible for the excavation or demolition, the starting date, anticipated duration and type of excavation or demolition operation to be conducted, the location of the proposed excavation or demolition, and whether or not explosives are to be used. 
(c)  If notification required by this section is made by telephone, an adequate record of such notification shall be maintained by the superintendent at the city hall. 
(Code 1984, § 6-3-4; Code 1996, § 90-145)  
Sec. 50-141. - Response to notice of intent. 
Each operator or designated representative notified in accordance with section 50-140 shall, not less than two working days in advance of the proposed excavation or demolition, unless a shorter period is provided by agreement between the person responsible for the excavation or demolition and the operator or designated representative, supply, by use of maps when appropriate, the following information to the person responsible for the excavation or demolition: 
(1)  The approximate location and description of all of its underground utilities which may be damaged as a result of the excavation or demolition; 
(2)  The location and description of all utility markers indicating the approximate location of the underground utilities; and 
(3)  Any other information that would assist that person in locating and thereby avoiding damage to the underground utilities, including providing adequate temporary marking indicating the approximate location of the underground utility in locations where permanent utility markers do not exist. 
(Code 1984, § 6-3-5; Code 1996, § 90-146)  
Sec. 50-142. - Emergency. 
Compliance with the notice requirements of section 50-140 is not required of persons responsible for emergency excavation or demolition to ameliorate an imminent danger to life, health or property; provided, however, that such persons give, as soon as practicable, oral notice of the emergency excavation or demolition to each operator having underground utilities located in the area where such excavation or demolition is to be performed and requests emergency assistance from each operator so identified in locating and providing immediate protection to its underground utilities. An imminent danger to life, health, or property exists whenever there is a substantial likelihood that loss of life, health, or property will result before the procedures under sections 50-140 and 50-141 can be fully complied with. 
(Code 1984, § 6-3-6; Code 1996, § 90-147)  
Sec. 50-143. - Damage. 
(a)  Except as provided by subsection (b) of this section, each person responsible for any excavation or demolition operation designated in section 50-139 that results in any damage to an underground utility shall, immediately upon discovery of such damage, notify the operator of such utility of the location and nature of the damage and shall allow the operator reasonable time to accomplish necessary repairs before completing the excavation or demolition in the immediate area of such utility. 
(b)  Each person responsible for any excavation or demolition operation designated in section 50-139 that results in damage to an underground utility permitting the escape of any flammable, toxic or corrosive gas or liquid shall, immediately upon discovery of such damage, notify the operator, police and fire departments, and take any other action as may be reasonably necessary to protect persons and property and to minimize the hazards until the arrival of the operator's personnel or police and fire departments. 
(Code 1984, § 6-3-8; Code 1996, § 90-148)  
Sec. 50-144. - Precautions to avoid damage. 
In addition to the notification requirements of section 50-140, each person responsible for any excavation or demolition operation designated in section 50-139 shall: 
(1)  Plan the excavation or demolition to avoid damage to or minimize interference with underground utilities in and near the construction area; 
(2)  Maintain a clearance between an underground utility and the cutting edge or point of any mechanized equipment, taking into account the known limit of control of such cutting edge or point, as may be reasonably necessary to avoid damage to such utility; and 
(3)  Provide such support for underground utilities in and near the construction area, including during backfill operations, as may be reasonably necessary for the protection of such utilities. 
(Code 1984, § 6-3-7; Code 1996, § 90-149)  
Secs. 50-145—50-171. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE V. - CATV FRANCHISE 
 
Sec. 50-172. - Fee per Consumer Choice for Television Act. 
The city shall collect a fee of five percent of the operator's gross revenues as provided by law, for any cable or video state franchise issued in the corporate boundaries by the state pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 36-76-1 et seq., known as the "Consumer Choice for Television Act" of 2007. 
(Res. of 7-1-2008)  
Chapter 52 - VEHICLES FOR HIRE  
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Secs. 52-1—52-18. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - TAXICABS  
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
 
Sec. 52-19. - Presumption of operation. 
Any automobile marked, labeled or identified by lettering or numbers as a taxicab and found upon the streets of the city, or regularly used for transportation of passengers, shall be presumed to be used as a taxicab and for transportation of passengers for hire, for the purpose of this article. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-47; Code 1996, § 94-31)  
Sec. 52-20. - Identification and marking of vehicles. 
(a)  All motor vehicles operated as taxicabs in the city shall be marked on the outside with the following information: 
(1)  The name of the owner; 
(2)  The word "taxicab" or "taxi"; 
(3)  If a fleet or more than one taxicab is operated by one company or owner, a number shall be assigned to each vehicle, which shall be individual and identifying; and 
(4)  Any other information which may be deemed necessary by the mayor and council. 
(b)  The markings described in subsection (a) of this section shall be stenciled or painted on each side of the taxicab in a permanent paint of contrasting color to the color of the vehicle or affixed by decal or some like manner. The letters of such markings shall not be less than three inches in height and must be printed so that the markings may be easily read at a distance of at least 50 feet. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-21; Code 1996, § 94-32)  
Sec. 52-21. - Certificate of vehicle inspection required. 
The owner and operator of each taxicab licensed to operate within the city shall, before having his license either granted or renewed, produce to the city manager a written inspection report from a qualified automobile mechanic engaged in business within the city. Such mechanic shall be approved by the mayor and council, showing that the brakes and lights on each unit operated by him are in safe, serviceable condition. The license shall in no case be granted until this section is complied with. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-22; Code 1996, § 94-33)  
Sec. 52-22. - Sale, trade or exchange of vehicle. 
(a)  Notice required. If any owner or operator of a taxicab in the city shall sell, trade or exchange any taxicab being operated in the city and substitute another car therefor, it shall be the duty of the seller to notify the city clerk within ten hours of the sale, trade or exchange of the vehicle, giving the number under which the car traded is identified in the policy of liability insurance on file with the mayor and council. 
(b)  Transfer of insurance required. It shall also be the duty of such owner or operator of the car substituted to furnish the clerk written endorsement of the insurance company issuing the public liability policy, the endorsement to be attached as an endorsement on the liability policy, showing that the car substituted is insured under the terms of the liability insurance. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-23; Code 1996, § 94-34)  
Sec. 52-23. - Drivers—Minimum age. 
No person shall drive a taxicab upon the streets of the city who is less than 19 years of age. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-24; Code 1996, § 94-35)  
Sec. 52-24. - Drivers—Effect of felony conviction. 
No person shall drive a taxicab upon the streets of the city who has been convicted of an offense constituting a felony or who has pleaded guilty upon a charge of having committed an offense constituting a felony. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-25; Code 1996, § 94-36)  
Sec. 52-25. - Drivers—Driving under influence of intoxicating liquor. 
It shall be unlawful for any person licensed to drive a taxicab under the provisions of this article to operate such taxicab while he is under the influence of intoxicating liquor. A violation of this section shall be grounds for license revocation. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-26; Code 1996, § 94-37)  
Sec. 52-26. - Transporting alcoholic beverages. 
(a)  Prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any person operating a licensed taxicab service in the city, or any driver operating a taxicab in the city under the license, to knowingly haul wine, liquor or beer in such taxicab, provided that this section shall not apply to a driver transporting a fare-paying passenger in possession of alcoholic beverages so long as such alcoholic beverages remain in the possession and control of the passenger and are not opened within the vehicle. 
(b)  Revocation of license. If the driver of any taxicab in the city knowingly allows or permits intoxicating liquor, wine or beer to be hauled in the taxicab operated by him in violation of this section, the license issued by the city shall automatically be revoked. If any license is forfeited and revoked because a driver is guilty of hauling intoxicating liquor, wine or beer, and desires to be heard, he shall have a right to appeal to the mayor and council for a hearing and be heard at such time and place as the mayor and council shall designate. Pending the hearing before the mayor and council, the licensee shall not operate the taxicab service under and by virtue of any such license. 
(c)  Forfeiture of driver's rights. It shall be unlawful for any driver guilty of knowingly hauling liquor, wine or beer in any taxicab driven by him to again drive a taxicab in the city. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-27; Code 1996, § 94-38)  
Sec. 52-27. - Number of passengers. 
No person shall drive a taxicab upon the streets of the city when such vehicle contains more persons than such vehicle is designed to carry. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-28; Code 1996, § 94-39)  
Sec. 52-28. - Receiving and discharging passengers. 
Drivers of taxicabs shall not receive or discharge passengers in the roadway but shall drive to the sidewalk or curb on the right-hand side of such roadway, and there receive or discharge passengers. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-29; Code 1996, § 94-40)  
Secs. 52-29—52-59. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 2. - OCCUPATIONAL LICENSE 
 
Sec. 52-60. - Required for drivers. 
It shall be unlawful to drive a taxicab or vehicle of any kind for the purpose of transporting passengers or property for hire without first applying for and obtaining an occupational license therefor. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-1; Code 1996, § 94-56)  
Sec. 52-61. - Required to engage in taxicab business. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of furnishing taxicab service in the city and maintaining a place of business in the city without first obtaining a license approved by the mayor and council. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-9; Code 1996, § 94-57)  
Sec. 52-62. - Application; manner and form. 
Application for a taxicab driver's license shall be made in such manner and form as prescribed by the city manager. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-2; Code 1996, § 94-58)  
Sec. 52-63. - Statement to accompany application. 
Application for a license to drive a taxicab shall be supported by a sworn statement of the applicant setting forth the following: 
(1)  Name and address of the applicant; 
(2)  The applicant's age; 
(3)  The applicant's habits as to sobriety; and 
(4)  Whether or not the applicant has been convicted of any offense against the laws of the state or of any city, and particularly whether or not he has been convicted of violating any traffic regulation of any state or city. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-3; Code 1996, § 94-59)  
Sec. 52-64. - Approval of application. 
No license shall be issued to drive a taxicab until the application has been approved by the city manager. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-4; Code 1996, § 94-60)  
Sec. 52-65. - Personal appearance of applicant. 
The applicant shall submit himself personally before the city manager, if required, or if he so desires, at the time the application for a taxicab driver's license is considered. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-5; Code 1996, § 94-61)  
Sec. 52-66. - Action on application; issuance and denial; fees. 
If, upon a consideration of an application for a license to drive a taxicab, the city manager shall decide that the applicant is qualified and entitled to operate a taxicab and in all manners in full compliance with all local, state and federal laws, having due regard to the safety and morals of the public, the application shall be granted and a license issued by the city clerk, upon payment of the business or occupation tax legally demandable. If the city manager shall determine that the applicant is not a fit and proper person to be so licensed, having due regard for the safety and morals of the public, the mayor and council shall refuse such license. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-6; Code 1996, § 94-62)  
Sec. 52-67. - Suspension or revocation authorized for good cause. 
(a)  The city manager shall have authority to suspend or revoke any and all licenses issued under this article, for good cause shown, or in the event the licensee fails to maintain compliance with any local, state or federal law relevant to the operation of the licensed business, after five days' notice given the licensee, at either a regular or special meeting. It shall be unlawful for any licensee to operate during the period of suspension. 
(b)  The term "good cause" shall mean any violation of this Code or of any state statutes pertaining to the operation of motor vehicles. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-10; Code 1996, § 94-65)  
Sec. 52-68. - Revocation for failure to provide service. 
It is the declared policy of the mayor and council that, in licensing the operation of vehicles under this article, a reasonable service will be rendered to the general public and to the inhabitants of the city by the persons holding those licenses, and if such service cannot or will not be rendered by any person holding such license, the license should be revoked. Among the causes justifying such revocation shall be unreasonable failure or refusal to render such service. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-12; Code 1996, § 94-67)  
Secs. 52-69—52-94. - Reserved.  
DIVISION 3. - INSURANCE 
 
Sec. 52-95. - Compliance with division required. 
It shall be unlawful to operate upon the public roads, streets and highways within the corporate limits of the city any taxicab which is subject to the regulations and ordinances of the city unless such operation is done in conformity to this division with respect to insurance protection. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-41; Code 1996, § 94-86)  
Sec. 52-96. - Coverage required. 
Before using or operating any taxicab which is subject to the provisions of this division for transporting passengers, and before allowing any other person to do so within the city upon the roads, streets and highways, the owner shall provide for each vehicle to be so used, and for the benefit of any and all persons having claims against the owner for damage by way of loss of life, damage to property, and/or for injury to the person, minimum liability insurance coverage as follows: 
Type of Coverage 	Amount 
Minimum personal injury coverage for injuries 	$100,000.00 
Minimum property damage coverage 	  50,000.00 
 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-42; Code 1996, § 94-87)  
Sec. 52-97. - Approval. 
Insurance coverage required by this division shall be subject to approval by the city manager and shall be with a company satisfactory to the city manager and in a form satisfactory to the city manager. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-43; Code 1996, § 94-88)  
Sec. 52-98. - Deposit of policies with city manager. 
It shall be the duty of the owner to deposit such policies with the city manager, where they shall remain while in force. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-44; Code 1996, § 94-89)  
Sec. 52-99. - Notice of cancellation required. 
It shall be the duty of the insurer to give reasonable notice to the city before cancelling any coverage. Any company failing to do so will not be considered an acceptable company for the purpose of furnishing such coverage. 
(Code 1984, § 9-3-45; Code 1996, § 94-90)  
Chapter 54 - ZONING[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— Zoning Procedures Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-66-1 et seq.; local government zoning powers, O.C.G.A. § 36-66-2; authority to adopt plans and exercise the power of zoning, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ IV. 
 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
 
Sec. 54-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Accessory use means a use customarily incidental, and subordinate to, the principal use or building and located on the same lot with such principal use or building. 
Advertising sign, outdoor, means a structural poster panel or painted sign, either freestanding or attached to the outside of a building, for the purpose of conveying information, knowledge, or ideas to the public about a subject either related or unrelated to the premises upon which located. 
Alteration means any change in the supporting members of a building (such as bearing walls, beams, columns or girders) except such change as may be required for its safety; any addition to a building; any change in use from that of one district classification to another; or any change of a building from one location to another. 
Building means any structure having a roof supported by columns or by walls and intended for shelter, housing or enclosure of persons, animals or chattels. The term "building" includes the term "structure." 
Building, accessory, means a building subordinate, or supplemental to, the main building on a lot and used for purposes customarily incidental to that of a main or principal building and located on the same lot therewith. 
Building, principal, means a building in which is conducted the main use of the lot on which the building is located. 
Business sign means an attached or freestanding structure which directs attention to a business or profession conducted on the premises. 
Centerline of street means the line surveyed and monumented by the mayor and council as such or, if a centerline has not been surveyed and monumented, it shall be that line running midway between the outside curbs or ditches of the street. 
Customary home occupation means an occupation or profession customarily carried on by an occupant of a dwelling unit as a secondary use which is clearly incidental to the dwelling unit for residential purposes, and carried on wholly within the principal building, and provided that not more than 30 percent of the floor area of the principal building is used for such purposes. 
Dwelling means a building designed, arranged, or used for a permanent living quarters for one or more persons. 
Dwelling unit means a building, or portion of a building, providing complete living facilities for one family. 
Family means one or more persons occupying a dwelling and living as a single house-keeping unit. 
Lot means a portion or parcel of land devoted to a common use or occupied by a building or group of buildings devoted to a common use, together with the customary accessories and open spaces belonging to the same. The term "lot" includes the term "plot" or "parcel." 
Lot, depth of, means the mean horizontal distance between the front and rear lot lines, measured in the general direction of the side lot lines. 
Lot, width of, means the distance between side lot lines measured at the building line. 
Map means the zoning map of the city on file in the office of the building official. 
Nonconforming use means a building, structure or use of land existing at the time of enactment of the ordinance from which this chapter was derived, and which does not conform to the regulations of the district in which it is located. 
Sight distance means the length of roadway visible to the driver of a passenger vehicle at any given point on the roadway when the view is unobstructed by traffic. 
Street means a public or private way which affords the principal means of access to abutting properties. 
Structure means anything constructed or erected, the use of which requires location on the ground, or attachment to something having location on the ground. 
Used or occupied, as applied to any land or building, includes the words "intended, arranged or designed to be used or occupied." 
Yard means a space on the same lot with a principal building open, unoccupied and unobstructed by buildings or structures from ground to sky, except where encroachments and accessory buildings are expressly permitted. 
Yard, front, means an open, unoccupied space on the same lot with a principal building, extending the full width of the lot, and situated between the street and the front line of the building projected to side lines of the lot. 
Yard, rear, means an open, unoccupied space on the same lot with a principal building, extending the full width of the lot and situated between the rear line of the lot and the rear line of the building projected to side lines of the lot. 
Yard, side, means an open, unoccupied space on the same lot with a principal building, situated between the building and the side lot line of the lot and extending from the front yard to the rear yard. Any lot line not a rear line or a front line shall be deemed a side line. 
(Code 1984, §§ 8-6-2, 8-6-3; Code 1996, § 98-1)  
Secs. 54-2—54-22. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE II. - ADMINISTRATION, ENFORCEMENT AND PENALTIES 
 
Sec. 54-23. - Zoning enforcement officer. 
The provisions of this chapter shall be administered and enforced by the building official. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-71; Code 1996, § 98-31)  
Sec. 54-24. - Invalidated without construction progress. 
Any building permit issued shall become invalid unless the work authorized by it shall have been commenced within six months of its date of issue or if the work authorized by it is suspended or abandoned for a period of one year. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-74; Code 1996, § 98-34)  
Sec. 54-25. - Certificate of occupancy required. 
(a)  A certificate of occupancy issued by the building official is required in advance of occupancy or use of: 
(1)  A building hereafter erected, altered or moved. 
(2)  A change of use of any building or land. 
(3)  Each nonconforming use created by the passage of and subsequent amendments to this chapter. Such nonconforming use shall obtain a certificate of occupancy within 30 days of the date of such passage or amendments. 
(b)  Upon payment of any required fees, the building official shall sign and issue a certificate of occupancy if the proposed use of land or building, as stated on the certificate of occupancy, is signed by the owner or his appointed agent, is found to conform to the applicable provisions of this chapter, and if the building, as finally constructed, complies with the plans submitted for the building permit. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-75; Code 1996, § 98-35)  
Sec. 54-26. - Denial of certificate of occupancy. 
A certificate of occupancy shall not be issued unless the proposed use of a building or land conforms to the applicable provisions of this chapter, or unless the building, as finally constructed, complies with the sketch or plan upon which the building permit was issued. The building official shall state in writing the reasons for denying such certificate of occupancy. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-76; Code 1996, § 98-36)  
Sec. 54-27. - Other remedies. 
In case any building is erected, constructed, reconstructed, altered, repaired, converted or maintained, or any building or land is used in violation of this chapter, the building official, or any other appropriate city authority, or any person who would be damaged by such violation, in addition to other remedies, may institute injunction, mandamus or other appropriate action in proceeding to prevent the violation in the case of each building or use of land. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-78; Code 1996, § 98-38)  
Secs. 54-28—54-57. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE III. - ESTABLISHMENT OF DISTRICTS 
 
Sec. 54-58. - Division into districts. 
For the purpose of this chapter, the city is divided into five districts designated as follows: 
(1)  R-A Residence District; 
(2)  R-B General Residence District; 
(3)  C-1 Central Business District; 
(4)  C-2 General Business District; and 
(5)  M Industrial District. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-11; Code 1996, § 98-66)  
Sec. 54-59. - District boundaries. 
The boundaries of each district are shown on a map entitled "Zoning Map for Donalsonville, Georgia," adopted September 24, 1962, as may be amended from time to time, and certified by the city clerk. Such map and all explanatory matter thereon accompanies and is hereby made a part of this chapter. The map shall be retained in the office of the city clerk. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-12; Code 1996, § 98-67) 
Editor's note— The zoning map is not included in this Code, but is on file in the office of the city clerk and is available for inspection during regular office hours.  
Sec. 54-60. - Map amendment. 
If, in accordance with the provisions of this chapter, changes are made in district boundaries or other subject matter portrayed on the zoning map, such change shall be made on the official zoning map promptly after the amendment has been approved by the mayor and council. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-13; Code 1996, § 98-68)  
Sec. 54-61. - Rules for determining boundaries. 
Where uncertainty exists with respect to the boundaries of any of the districts enumerated in section 54-58 and as shown on the zoning map, the following rules shall apply: 
(1)  Where district boundaries are indicated as approximately following the centerlines of streets or highways, street lines, or highway right-of-way lines, such centerlines, street lines, or highway right-of-way lines shall be construed to be the boundaries. 
(2)  Where district boundaries are so indicated that they approximately follow the lot lines, such lot lines shall be construed to be the boundaries. 
(3)  Where district boundaries are so indicated that they are approximately parallel to the centerlines of streets, highways or railroads, or rights-of-way of same, such district boundaries shall be construed as being parallel thereto and at such distance therefrom as indicated on the zoning map. If no distance is given, such dimension shall be determined by the use of the scale shown on the zoning map. 
(4)  Where a district boundary line, as appearing on the zoning map, divides a lot in single ownership at the time of this enactment, the district requirements for the least restricted portion of such lot shall be deemed to apply to the whole thereof, provided that such extensions shall not include any part of such a lot more than 35 feet beyond the district boundary line. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-14; Code 1996, § 98-69)  
Secs. 54-62—54-80. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE IV. - APPLICATION OF REGULATIONS 
 
Sec. 54-81. - Use. 
Except as provided in this chapter, no building, structure or land shall hereafter be used or occupied, and no building or structure or part thereof shall hereafter be erected, constructed, reconstructed, moved or structurally altered unless in conformity with all of the regulations specified in this chapter for the district in which it is located. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-21; Code 1996, § 98-96)  
Sec. 54-82. - Height and density. 
Except as provided in this chapter, no building or other structure shall hereafter be erected or altered to: 
(1)  Exceed the height limits; 
(2)  Accommodate or house a greater number of families or occupy a smaller lot area per family; or 
(3)  Have narrower or smaller rear yards, front yards, side yards or other open spaces than are required or specified in this chapter; or in any other manner contrary to the provisions of this chapter. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-22; Code 1996, § 98-97)  
Sec. 54-83. - Yard service to one building. 
Except as provided in this chapter, no part of a yard, or other open space, or off-street parking or loading space required about, or in connection with, any building for the purpose of complying with this chapter, shall be included as part of a yard, open space, or off-street parking or loading space similarly required for any other building. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-23; Code 1996, § 98-98)  
Sec. 54-84. - One principal building per lot. 
Except as provided in this chapter, every building or structure hereafter erected shall be located on a lot or tract. There shall not be more than one principal building on one lot, plus its approved accessory buildings, except as provided in section 54-179. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-24; Code 1996, § 98-99)  
Sec. 54-85. - Reduction of lot area. 
Except as provided in this chapter, no lot, even though it may consist of one or more adjacent lots of record, shall be reduced in size so that the lot width or depth, front, side or rear yard, lot area per family or other requirements of this chapter are not maintained. This section shall not apply when a portion of a lot is acquired for public purposes. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-25; Code 1996, § 98-100)  
Sec. 54-86. - Street frontage. 
Except as provided in this chapter, no principal building shall be erected on any lot which does not have immediate frontage on at least one street for a distance of not less than 25 feet. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-26; Code 1996, § 98-101)  
Sec. 54-87. - Corner lots. 
Except as provided in this chapter, minimum side yard requirements for corner lots shall be not less than the minimum front yard requirements for such lots. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-27; Code 1996, § 98-102)  
Secs. 54-88—54-117. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE V. - PROVISIONS APPLICABLE TO ALL DISTRICTS 
 
Sec. 54-118. - Classification of streets. 
For the purpose of this chapter, all streets in the city are hereby divided into three classes: 
(1)  Major streets; 
(2)  Collector streets; and 
(3)  Minor streets. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-41; Code 1996, § 98-131)  
Sec. 54-119. - Continuance of a nonconforming use. 
Any building, structure or use of land existing at the time of the enactment of the ordinance from which this chapter was derived, or subsequent amendment of this chapter, but not in conformity with its use regulations and provisions may be continued with the following limitations. Such building, structure or use shall not be: 
(1)  Changed to another nonconforming use; 
(2)  Extended or enlarged, except in conformity with this chapter; 
(3)  Re-established after discontinuance for one year; or 
(4)  Rebuilt, altered, or repaired after damage exceeding 75 percent of its assessed value for city tax purposes. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-42; Code 1996, § 98-132)  
Sec. 54-120. - Off-street automobile parking or storage. 
(a)  Off-street automobile parking or storage space shall be provided on every lot on which any of the following uses are hereafter established; or, provided no space is available on the lot, such space shall be provided within 500 feet of such uses. Off-street automobile parking or storage space shall be provided with vehicular access to a street or alley and shall be equal in area to at least the minimum requirements for the specific use as set forth in this section. 
Off-Street Automobile Parking or Storage Minimum Requirements 
Use Classification 	Minimum Requirements 
Any residential structure 	One space for each four seats in the main assembly room. 
Roominghouses and boardinghouses, hotels 	One space for each two rooms. 
Churches, fraternal organizations, and other places of public assembly 	One space for each four seats in the main assembly room. 
Tourist homes, tourist courts or motels 	One space for each accommodation. 
Hospitals, nursing homes or similar institutions 	One space for each two beds intended for patients, plus one space for each three employees. 
Retail businesses 	One space for each 250 square feet of total floor area. 
Offices, including banks 	One space for each 300 square feet of total floor space. 
Filling stations 	Two spaces for each gas pump, plus three spaces for each grease rack or similar facility. 
Wholesaling 	One space for each two employees. 
Industrial 	One space for each two employees at maximum employment on a single shift. 
 
(b)  For the purpose of this chapter, a parking or storage space shall not be less than 200 square feet of area with appropriate dimensions for the parking of an automobile, excluding all driveways and entrances and exits. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-43; Code 1996, § 98-133)  
Sec. 54-121. - Off-street loading and unloading space. 
Every building or structure used for business, trade or industry shall provide space, as indicated in this section, for the loading and unloading of vehicles off the street or public alley. Such space shall have access to an alley or if there is no alley, to a street. 
Off-Street Loading and Unloading Space Minimum Requirements 
Use Classification 	Minimum Requirements 
Retail businesses 	One space of 300 square feet for each 3,000 square feet of floor area. 
Wholesale and industry 	One space of 550 square feet for each 10,000 square feet of floor area. 
Bus and truck terminals 	Sufficient space to accommodate the maximum number of buses or trucks to be stored or to be loading or unloading at the terminal at any one time. 
 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-44; Code 1996, § 98-134)  
Secs. 54-122—54-140. - Reserved.  
ARTICLE VI. - USE REQUIREMENTS BY DISTRICTS 
 
Sec. 54-141. - Residence District (R-A). 
Within an R-A Residence District, the following uses shall be permitted: 
(1)  Single-family residences, but not including residential trailers. 
(2)  Two-family residences. 
(3)  Churches and their customary related uses, provided that they: 
a.  Are located on a lot fronting a major or collector street; and 
b.  Are placed not less than 50 feet from any property line and are separated from such property line by a planted buffer strip at least ten feet wide. 
(4)  Public and private schools offering general education courses. 
(5)  Municipal, county, state, federal and other public uses, including parks and playgrounds. 
(6)  Accessory uses and customary home occupations, including professional offices of a doctor, dentist, lawyer, architect or similar use, provided that such uses and occupations shall be conducted within a principal building and that not more than 30 percent of the floor area of the principal building shall be used for such purpose. There shall be no external evidence of such use except a non-illuminated identification sign not exceeding two square feet in area. 
(7)  Accessory buildings, provided such shall be permitted only in a rear yard and shall not be less than five feet from any property line. 
(8)  Golf courses and private clubs of not less than 40 acres. 
(9)  Public utility stations, such as electrical substations, sewage pumping stations, etc., if such stations are essential for the service of the immediate area and subject to the following conditions: Such uses shall be enclosed within a woven wire fence not less than four feet high; and shall be suitably landscaped and the storage of vehicles and equipment on the premises shall be prohibited. 
(10)  Special home occupations. 
a.  Includes mail and online sales occupations and activities when conducted entirely within a dwelling and/or accessory building only by the residents thereof, which is clearly incidental and secondary to the use of the dwelling and/or accessory building for residential purposes and does not change the character thereof, as may be lawfully established under the terms of this zoning ordinance. 
b.  General provisions. In districts where permitted, the following regulations shall apply: 
1.  The total gross floor area of a dwelling unit devoted to a special home occupation shall not exceed 750 square feet or 25 percent of the gross floor space of the dwelling, whichever is less. An accessory building used for a special home occupation shall be constructed entirely in accordance with and meet all applicable building codes and regulations. Portable buildings (non-stick-built buildings constructed off-site) cannot be used in conjunction with a special home occupation. 
2.  The exterior appearances of the dwelling or accessory building must remain that of a dwelling or accessory building to a dwelling. No internal or external alternations inconsistent with the residential use of the buildings may be permitted. 
3.  Vehicles kept on site in association with the special home occupation shall be used by residents only. Only vehicles used primarily as passenger vehicles shall be permitted in connection with the conduct of the special home occupation. 
4.  No special home occupation shall generate traffic, sound, smell, vibration, light or dust that is offensive or that creates a nuisance. No equipment that interferes with radio, television or other wireless reception shall be allowed. Chemical, electrical or mechanical equipment that is not normally a part of domestic or household equipment and which is used primarily for commercial purposes shall not be permitted. 
5.  No patrons or customers shall be allowed to visit the dwelling and/or accessory building where the special home occupation is conducted for the purpose of conducting either wholesale or retail business transactions. 
6.  There shall be no display, and no stock-in-trade, nor commodity sold or stored on the premises, in connection with a special home occupation. 
7.  There shall be no signs permitted on the premises in conjunction with a special home occupation. 
8.  Only occupants of the dwelling where the special home occupation is conducted shall be authorized to work on the premises in connection with a special home occupation. Any occupational licenses, including business registrations, required by state or city regulations must be obtained. Proof of state and/or federal registration, if required, for the special home occupation shall be submitted to the city prior to the issuance of a business registration. 
9.  In as much as the special home occupation permit is designed expressly for the purpose of allowing mail order or online sales in compliance with this section within residential districts, all other business of any type or kind are prohibited from applying for or receiving a special home occupation permit. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-51; Code 1996, § 98-161; Ord. of 11-3-2009(1), § 98-161)  
Sec. 54-142. - General Residence District (R-B). 
Within an R-B General Residence District, the following uses shall be permitted: 
(1)  All uses permitted in R-A Residence Districts. 
(2)  Multifamily residences. 
(3)  Roominghouses and boardinghouses. 
(4)  Tourist homes. 
(5)  Clubs and lodges. 
(6)  Nursery schools or kindergartens, provided that they shall have at least 100 square feet of outdoor play area and at least 35 square feet of indoor space provided for each child; the outdoor play area shall be enclosed by a fence having a height of at least three feet, six inches; and provided that the principal building of such use shall meet all the yard requirements of this R-B District. 
(7)  Trailer parks, provided the parks meet the requirements of the city code regulating such use. 
(8)  Special home occupations. 
a.  Includes mail and online sales occupations and activities when conducted entirely within a dwelling and/or accessory building only by the residents thereof, which is clearly incidental and secondary to the use of the dwelling and/or accessory building for residential purposes and does not change the character thereof, as may be lawfully established under the terms of this zoning ordinance. 
b.  General provisions. In districts where permitted, the following regulations shall apply: 
1.  The total gross floor area of a dwelling unit devoted to a special home occupation shall not exceed 750 square feet or 25 percent of the gross floor space of the dwelling, whichever is less. An accessory building used for a special home occupation shall be constructed entirely in accordance with and meet all applicable building codes and regulations. Portable buildings (non-stick-built buildings constructed off-site) cannot be used in conjunction with a special home occupation. 
2.  The exterior appearances of the dwelling or accessory building must remain that of a dwelling or accessory building to a dwelling. No internal or external alternations inconsistent with the residential use of the buildings may be permitted. 
3.  Vehicles kept on site in association with the special home occupation shall be used by residents only. Only vehicles used primarily as passenger vehicles shall be permitted in connection with the conduct of the special home occupation. 
4.  No special home occupation shall generate traffic, sound, smell, vibration, light or dust that is offensive or that creates a nuisance. No equipment that interferes with radio, television or other wireless reception shall be allowed. Chemical, electrical or mechanical equipment that is not normally a part of domestic or household equipment and which is used primarily for commercial purposes shall not be permitted. 
5.  No patrons or customers shall be allowed to visit the dwelling and/or accessory building where the special home occupation is conducted for the purpose of conducting either wholesale or retail business transactions. 
6.  There shall be no display, and no stock-in-trade, nor commodity sold or stored on the premises, in connection with a special home occupation. 
7.  There shall be no signs permitted on the premises in conjunction with a special home occupation. 
8.  Only occupants of the dwelling where the special home occupation is conducted shall be authorized to work on the premises in connection with a special home occupation. Any occupational licenses, including business registrations, required by state or city regulations must be obtained. Proof of state and/or federal registration, if required, for the special home occupation shall be submitted to the city prior to the issuance of a business registration. 
9.  In as much as the special home occupation permit is designed expressly for the purpose of allowing mail order or online sales in compliance with this section within residential districts, all other business of any type or kind are prohibited from applying for or receiving a special home occupation permit. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-52; Code 1996, § 98-162; Ord. of 11-3-2009(1), § 98-161)  
Sec. 54-143. - Central Business District (C-1). 
Within a C-1 Central Business District, the following uses shall be permitted: 
(1)  Any retail business or service establishment, including the making of articles sold at retail on the premises, provided such manufacturing is incidental to the retail business or service, occupies less than 40 percent of the floor area, and employs no more than five persons. 
(2)  Hotels, offices and banks. 
(3)  Railroad stations. 
(4)  Parking lots. 
(5)  Public utility stations. 
(6)  Newspaper offices and printing establishments. 
(7)  Attached outdoor advertising signs and business signs. 
(8)  City, county, state and federal uses and buildings. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-53; Code 1996, § 98-163)  
Sec. 54-144. - General Business District (C-2). 
Within a C-2 General Business District, the following uses shall be permitted: 
(1)  All uses permitted in a C-1 Central Business District. 
(2)  Bus and truck terminals. 
(3)  Auto sales and repair services. 
(4)  Funeral parlors. 
(5)  Parking lots. 
(6)  Dry cleaning plants. 
(7)  Filling stations, provided that all structures and buildings, except principal use signs, and including storage tanks, shall be placed not less than 25 feet from any side or rear property line, except where such side or rear property lines abut a street, in which case the setback shall be that required for such streets measured from the centerline. All buildings or structures, including gas pumps and storage tanks, except principal use signs, shall comply with the setback requirements of any abutting street. If on a corner lot, the means of ingress and egress shall be provided not less than 15 feet from the intersection of street lines. Ingress and egress shall be arranged and designed so as to minimize the interference with the flow of traffic. 
(8)  Wholesaling. 
(9)  Soft drink bottling and distribution plants. 
(10)  Baking establishments. 
(11)  Tourist courts and motels. 
(12)  Incidental or accessory advertising signs. 
(13)  Drive-in theaters, provided that there shall be not less than 200 feet of sight distance at any exit onto a major or collector street, and provided that there shall be off-street storage space to accommodate waiting automobiles at the ratio of one space for each three theater accommodations. 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-54; Code 1996, § 98-164)  
Sec. 54-145. - Industrial District (M). 
Within an M Industrial District, the following uses shall be permitted: 
(1)  Any retail or service establishment dependent or closely related to industry. 
(2)  Any industry which does not cause injurious or obnoxious noise, vibrations, smoke, gas, fumes, odor, dust, fire hazard or other objectionable conditions. 
(3)  Storage yards, including building materials and lumberyards, provided any such use is screened from view by a solid wall, planted screen or similar opaque partition at least six feet in height. Such partition shall comply with all setback requirements of the M District. 
(4)  Truck terminals. 
(5)  Wholesaling and warehousing. 
(6)  Junkyards, provided any such use is screened from view by a solid wall, planted screen or similar opaque partition at least six feet in height. Such partition shall comply with all setback requirements of the M District. 
(7)  Filling stations, provided that they meet all regulations as set forth in section 54-144(7). 
(8)  Signs, including outdoor advertising, incidental or accessory advertising, and business signs. 
(9)  Drive-in theaters, provided that they meet all regulations as set forth in section 54-144(13). 
(Code 1984, § 8-6-55; Code 1996, § 98-165)  
Sec. 54-146. - Area, yard and height regulations. 
Area, yard and height requirements for the various districts shall be as follows:
